Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
6 min
Jihad: Initial Ruling as Fard Kifayah
Opens jihad chapter, states ruling and stages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the initial ruling of jihad as fard kifayah and identify the conditions under which the Imam must launch expeditions.

Core Idea
Jihad is a collective obligation, not supererogatory; the Imam must lead expeditions yearly if strength permits.

This lesson introduces the chapter on jihad from a classical Hanafi fiqh manual. The passage establishes the fundamental ruling: when Muslims initiate warfare, jihad is a fard kifayah (collective obligation). Understanding this classification and its practical implications is crucial for grasping the Hanafi legal framework of armed conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text explicitly states 'huwa fard kifayah bad'an' – jihad is a collective obligation when initiated by Muslims.
This is the initial ruling; it becomes fard ayn in defensive situations.
2
Define jihad legally
Jihad means exerting effort; legally, it is calling to the true religion and fighting those who reject it after invitation.
The lexical and legal definitions are distinguished in the commentary.
3
Trace the historical stages
The command to fight came in stages: proclamation, argumentation, permission, then absolute command after initial prohibition during sacred months.
This shows the gradual legislation of jihad.
4
Identify practical obligations
The Imam must send a detachment to dar al-harb once or twice a year; the community must assist unless kharaj suffices. Failure burdens the Imam with sin.
The obligation is collective; the community shares responsibility if not fulfilled.
5
Note the condition of strength
Offensive jihad is only permissible if the Muslims have a reasonable expectation of overcoming the enemy (ghalabat al-zann).
Without this condition, jihad is not permitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجهاد (هو فرض كفاية بدءاً) (۱) : أي ابتداء ، وهو أن يبتدأ المسلمون بمحاربة الكفار [١] قوله : كتاب الجهاد ؛ لما فَرَغَ عن بحث الحدود وما يتعلق بها شرع في بحث الجهاد، وقدّم الأوّل على الثاني ؛ لكون المقصود من الحدود إخلاء العالم عن الفساد ومن الفسق ، والمقصود من الجهاد رفع فساد الكفر ؛ ولأن الحدود أكثر وقوعاً، وبعضها حق العبد، والجهاد حق الله حالة ، وهو - بكسر الجيم ، مصدر جاهد ؛ أي بذل وسعه. واستعمل شرعاً في الدعاء إلى الدين الحق وقتال من لم يقبله، وقد وردت في فضله أحاديث كثيرة، وقد كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مأموراً أولاً بالتبليغ والإعراض بقوله : فَأَصْدَعْ بِمَا تُؤْمَرُ وَأَعْرِضْ عَنِ الْمُشْرِكِينَ ) (٢). ثم أمر بالمجادلة بقوله : ادْعُ إِلَى سَبِيلِ رَبِّكَ بِالْحِكْمَةِ وَالْمَوْعِظَةِ الْحَسَنَةِ وَجَدِلْهُم بِالَّتِي هِيَ أَحْسَنُ (۳) ، ثم أذن له بالقتال بقوله لا : أُذِنَ لِلَّذِينَ يقتلون ) ، وقد كان القتالُ ممنوعاً في الأشهر الحرم في أوّل الإسلام، ثم أمر به مطلقاً، كذا في «شرح السير الكبير» لشمس الائمة السَّرَخْسِي. [٢] قوله : هو فرض كفاية ؛ بالإضافة أو برفع فرض مع التنوين، ونصب كفاية معه ، قال في «الدر المنتقى»: وليس بتطوّع أصلاً، هو الصحيح، فيجب على الإمام أن يبعث سرية إلى دار الحرب كل سنة مرة أو مرتين وعلى الرعية إعانته إلا إذا أخذ الخراج فإن لم يبعث كان كل الإثم عليه، وهذا إذا غلب على ظنه أنه يكافئهم، وإلا فلا يباح قتالهم بخلاف الأمر بالمعروف . ينظر : «الدر المنتقى (١ : ٦٣٢).
The Book of Jihad. It is a collective obligation initially: that is, at the beginning, which is that the Muslims initiate warfare against the disbelievers. Commentary: The Book of Jihad; since he finished discussing hudud and what pertains to them, he began discussing jihad, and he placed the first before the second because the purpose of hudud is to rid the world of corruption and immorality, and the purpose of jihad is to remove the corruption of disbelief; and because hudud occur more frequently, and some of them are the right of the slave, while jihad is purely the right of Allah. Jihad—with a kasra on the jim—is the verbal noun of jāhada, meaning to exert one's effort. It is used legally for calling to the true religion and fighting those who do not accept it. Many hadiths have come regarding its virtue. The Prophet (peace be upon him) was first commanded to convey and turn away by His saying: 'So proclaim what you are commanded and turn away from the polytheists' (Quran 15:94). Then he was commanded to argue by His saying: 'Invite to the way of your Lord with wisdom and good instruction, and argue with them in the best way' (Quran 16:125). Then he was given permission to fight by His saying: 'Permission [to fight] has been given to those who are being fought' (Quran 22:39). And fighting was prohibited during the sacred months at the beginning of Islam, then it was commanded absolutely, as mentioned in Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir by Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi. Commentary: 'It is fard kifayah'—either with idafah (construct) or with raf' of fard with tanwin and nasb of kifayah with it. It is stated in al-Durr al-Muntaqa: 'It is not a supererogatory act at all; that is the correct view. So it is obligatory upon the Imam to send a detachment to the abode of war once or twice every year, and upon the subjects to assist him, unless he takes kharaj. If he does not send, then the entire sin is upon him. This applies if he is confident of being able to overcome them; otherwise, fighting them is not permissible, unlike commanding good.' See al-Durr al-Muntaqa (1:632).
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on jihad. The ruling is that jihad is initially a fard kifayah (collective obligation), meaning when Muslims initiate warfare against disbelievers. The commentator explains the precedence of discussing hudud over jihad, citing that hudud are more frequent and involve individual rights, while jihad is a communal right of Allah. The lexical meaning of jihad is exertion; legally it means calling to the true religion and fighting those who reject it after being called. The historical stages are outlined: first, proclamation and turning away; then argumentation; then permission to fight; finally, absolute command, with initial prohibition during sacred months. The relied-upon position from al-Durr al-Muntaqa emphasizes that jihad is not a supererogatory act but an obligation. Consequently, the Imam must send an expedition at least once or twice a year, and the community must support him, unless kharaj tax is sufficient. If he fails to do so, the sin is on him. However, this is conditional upon reasonable expectation of success; otherwise, offensive jihad is not permissible.

Key Terms
جهاد (jihad): Exerting effort; legally: calling to the true religion and fighting those who reject it after invitation.
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A religious obligation that, if performed by a sufficient number of the community, removes the obligation from others; otherwise, all who knew of it are sinful.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): The territory of war; lands under non-Muslim rule where Islamic law is not enforced.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the initial ruling of jihad when Muslims begin warfare?
A) Fard ayn
B) Fard kifayah
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Jihad is initially a fard kifayah, obligating the Imam to send expeditions yearly if success is likely, with the community's support.

Jihad as a Communal Obligation and Exemptions
Defining jihad as communal obligation and listing exempt persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that jihad is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) and identify the six categories of people exempt from this initial obligation, citing the Quranic proofs.

Core Idea
Jihad is a communal duty, not an individual one—unless the community itself is attacked.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies the nature of jihad: it is not a supererogatory act but a communal obligation (fard kifayah). When some Muslims fulfill it, the rest are absolved. However, certain individuals are exempt due to incapacity or legal status. The text provides the evidence from Quran and Sunnah for these rulings. Understanding this classification prevents the common mistake of treating jihad as either optional or unconditionally obligatory on every single Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its category
The author states that jihad is 'فرض كفاية بدءاً'. Identify what this means and how it differs from fard 'ayn.
Fard kifayah: obligation on every individual but falls when some perform it.
2
Locate the conditions for obligation
The Imam must ensure that the Muslims have capability to match the enemy. What does 'غلب على ظنه أنه يكافئهم' mean? How does this condition affect the obligation?
Without capability, initiating jihad is not permissible.
3
List the exempt individuals
The text lists six categories. Name them and note the reasoning for each based on the commentary.
Exempt: minor, slave, woman, blind, cripple, amputee.
4
Connect the exemptions to the Quranic proofs
Which verses are cited? How do they support the exemption of the disabled? And the hadith about women?
Quran 24:61 and 4:95 are the primary proofs.
5
Determine the thamarah
What is the practical effect of these exemptions? How does fard kifayah operate in a community?
The obligation rests on the community, not every individual.

كتاب الجهاد
هو فرض كفاية بدءاً : أي ابتداء، وهو أن يبتدأ المسلمون بمحاربة الكفار
[1] قوله : كتاب الجهاد ؛ لما فَرَغَ عن بحث الحدود وما يتعلق بها شرع في بحث الجهاد، وقدّم الأوّل على الثاني ؛ لكون المقصود من الحدود إخلاء العالم عن الفساد ومن الفسق ، والمقصود من الجهاد رفع فساد الكفر ؛ ولأن الحدود أكثر وقوعاً، وبعضها حق العبد، والجهاد حق الله حالة ، وهو - بكسر الجيم ، مصدر جاهد ؛ أي بذل وسعه. واستعمل شرعاً في الدعاء إلى الدين الحق وقتال من لم يقبله، وقد وردت في فضله أحاديث كثيرة، وقد كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مأموراً أولاً بالتبليغ والإعراض بقوله : فَأَصْدَعْ بِمَا تُؤْمَرُ وَأَعْرِضْ عَنِ الْمُشْرِكِينَ ) (٢). ثم أمر بالمجادلة بقوله : ادْعُ إِلَى سَبِيلِ رَبِّكَ بِالْحِكْمَةِ وَالْمَوْعِظَةِ الْحَسَنَةِ وَجَدِلْهُم بِالَّتِي هِيَ أَحْسَنُ (۳) ، ثم أذن له بالقتال بقوله لا : أُذِنَ لِلَّذِينَ يقتلون ) ، وقد كان القتالُ ممنوعاً في الأشهر الحرم في أوّل الإسلام، ثم أمر به مطلقاً، كذا في «شرح السير الكبير» لشمس الائمة السَّرَخْسِي.
[٢] قوله : هو فرض كفاية ؛ بالإضافة أو برفع فرض مع التنوين، ونصب كفاية معه ، قال في «الدر المنتقى»: وليس بتطوّع أصلاً، هو الصحيح، فيجب على الإمام أن يبعث سرية إلى دار الحرب كل سنة مرة أو مرتين وعلى الرعية إعانته إلا إذا أخذ الخراج فإن لم يبعث كان كل الإثم عليه، وهذا إذا غلب على ظنه أنه يكافئهم، وإلا فلا يباح قتالهم بخلاف الأمر بالمعروف . ينظر : «الدر المنتقى (١ : ٦٣٢). (٢) الحجر : ٩٤ . (۳) النحل : من الآية ١٢٥ . (٤) الحج : من الآية ٣٩.
إن قام به البعض سقط عن الباقين فإن تركوا أثموا إلا على صبي، وعبد، وامرأة، وأعمى، ومقعد، وأقطع.
[٣] قوله : إن قام ؛ هذه الجملة كالتفسير لفرض الكفاية.
[٢] قوله : سقط ؛ فيه إشارة إلى أنّ فرضَ الكفاية يكون فرضاً على كل واحد ، لكن يسقط عن الباقين بفعل بعضهم ؛ لحصول المقصود، وتحقيقه في كتب الأصول.
[٣] قوله : إلا على صبي ... الخ ؛ عدم افتراضه على الصبي لكونه من غير المكلفين لا يخاطب بسائر الفرائض ، ومثله المجنون، وعدمه على العبد لحق المولى، فإنّ حق العبدِ مقدم ، فلو أذن له المولى افترض عليه، وعدمه على المرأة لكونها ليست من أهله لضعف بنيتها ، وقيل : لحق الزوج. ومفاده الافتراض على غير المتزوجة، وعلى المتزوجة بإذن الزوج، والصحيح هو الوجه الأول، وقد ثبت في صحيح البخاري» وغيره : «إنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا ذهب إلى الغزو ذهبت معه بعض النِّساء، فكنّ يخدمن المرضى ويداوين الجرحى»، ولم يكن يلزم عليهن الذهاب معه ، ولا القتال. وكذا أصحاب الأعذار والمرضى لا يفترض عليهم ؛ لقوله : لَيْسَ عَلَى الْأَعْمَى حَرَجٌ وَلَا عَلَى الْأَعْرَجِ حَرَجٌ وَلَا عَلَى الْمَرِيضِ حَرَحُ ) ، وقوله : لَا يَسْتَوِى القَيدُونَ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ غَيْرُ أُولى الضَّرَرِ وَالجَهدُونَ فِي سَبيل الله ) (٣) الآية.
[٤] قوله : ومقعد ؛ على صيغة اسم المفعول، هو من أقعـد الـداء عن الحركة، وقيل : هو الزمن ، وقيل : مُتَشَنّج الأعضاء ، وقيل : هو الأعرج، كذا في «المغرب»(٤) ، و«الفتح».
The Book of Jihad. It is a communal obligation initially: meaning starting, and that is that Muslims begin to fight the disbelievers. [1] His statement: 'The Book of Jihad'; because when he finished discussing the Hadd punishments and what pertains to them, he began to discuss jihad. He gave precedence to the first over the second because the purpose of Hadd punishments is to rid the world of corruption and sin, and the purpose of jihad is to remove the corruption of disbelief; and because Hadd punishments occur more frequently, and some of them are rights of the servant, while jihad is solely a right of Allah. It is with a kasra on the jim, the masdar of jāhada, meaning to exert one's capacity. It is used in the Sharia to mean calling to the true religion and fighting those who do not accept it. Many hadiths have been narrated concerning its virtue. The Prophet, peace be upon him, was first commanded to convey and turn away by His saying: 'So proclaim what you are commanded and turn away from the polytheists' (Quran 15:94). Then he was commanded to debate by His saying: 'Invite to the way of your Lord with wisdom and good instruction, and argue with them in the way that is best' (Quran 16:125). Then he was permitted to fight by His saying: 'Permission [to fight] has been given to those who are being fought' (Quran 22:39). Fighting was prohibited during the sacred months at the beginning of Islam, then it was commanded absolutely. This is in Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi. [2] His statement: 'It is a communal obligation' – whether with idafa or raising 'fard' with tanwin and nasb of 'kifayah'. He said in al-Durr al-Muntaqa: 'It is not a supererogatory act at all; this is correct. The Imam must send a military detachment to the abode of war once or twice every year, and the subjects must assist him unless the kharaj is collected. If he does not send, all the sin is upon him. This is if he overwhelmingly thinks that they can match them; otherwise, fighting them is not permissible, unlike commanding the good.' Reference: al-Durr al-Muntaqa (1:632). (2) Quran 15:94. (3) Quran 16:125. (4) Quran 22:39. If some perform it, it falls from the rest; if they all abandon it, they sin, except for a minor, a slave, a woman, a blind person, a cripple, and an amputee. [3] His statement: 'If some perform' – this sentence is an explanation of 'communal obligation'. [2] His statement: 'falls' – it indicates that a communal obligation is an obligation on every individual, but it falls from the rest by the action of some because the purpose is achieved. Its verification is in books of usul. [3] His statement: 'except for a minor...etc.' – it is not obligatory on the minor because he is not among the legally responsible; he is not addressed with other obligations. Similarly, the insane. Its non-obligation on the slave is due to the right of the master, for the right of the servant takes precedence. If the master gives him permission, it becomes obligatory on him. Its non-obligation on the woman is because she is not of its people due to weakness of her constitution; it is said due to the right of the husband. Its implication is obligation on the unmarried woman, and on the married woman with the permission of her husband. The correct view is the first one. It is established in Sahih al-Bukhari and elsewhere that the Prophet, when he went for a military expedition, some women would go with him; they would serve the sick and treat the wounded. They were not required to go with him or to fight. Similarly, those with excuses and the sick are not obligated upon them due to His saying: 'There is no blame upon the blind nor any blame upon the lame nor any blame upon the sick' (Quran 24:61), and His saying: 'Not equal are those believers who sit [at home] – other than the disabled – and those who strive in the cause of Allah' (Quran 4:95) etc. [4] His statement: 'and a cripple' – on the form of the passive participle; it is one whom illness has disabled from movement. It is said: the one confined to bed; it is said: the one with contracted limbs; it is said: the lame. This is in al-Mughrib and al-Fath.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the obligation of jihad in the Hanafi school. The text begins by stating that jihad is فرض كفاية (a communal obligation) when initiated by Muslims. The commentary elaborates that this means it is not a supererogatory act; rather, it is an obligation that, if performed by some, absolves the rest. However, if everyone neglects it, all sin. The commentator highlights that the Imam must send an expedition at least once a year if the Muslims have the capability to match the enemy—otherwise, it is not permissible. This condition reflects the principle that jihad is not a reckless act but a strategic one. Then the text lists six categories of people who are not initially obligated: minors (non-mukallaf), slaves (due to the master's right), women (due to physical weakness or spousal rights), the blind, the crippled, and those with amputations. The commentary explains the reasoning for each: minors and the insane are not legally responsible; slaves are exempt unless their master permits; women are exempt but may accompany to serve, as proven by hadith from Bukhari; the disabled and sick are exempt based on Quranic verses (24:61, 4:95). The passage ends with a linguistic note on 'مقعد' (cripple). The overall structure follows the matn with interlinear commentary, typical of the Sharh al-Wiqayah tradition.

Key Terms
الجهاد (al-jihad): بذل الوسع في الدعاء إلى الدين الحق وقتال من لم يقبله (exertion of effort in calling to the true religion and fighting those who do not accept it)
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): فرض على كل واحد يسقط عن الباقين بفعل بعضهم (an obligation on every individual that falls from the rest when performed by some)
مقعد (muq'ad): المريض أو الزمن أو متشنج الأعضاء أو الأعرج (one confined to bed, disabled, with contracted limbs, or lame)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the six categories of people exempted from the initial obligation of jihad in the Hanafi school?
A) A minor (صبي)
B) A slave (عبد)
C) A wealthy merchant (تاجر غني)
D) A blind person (أعمى)

Key Takeaway
Jihad is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) that requires capability and leadership; those with legal incapacity or physical disability are exempt.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
8 min
Jihad as Fard Kifayah and Exempted Persons
Explains fard kifayah rule of jihad and lists exempted categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the categories of persons exempt from the obligation of jihad and explain the Hanafi ruling that jihad is fard kifayah, using the proofs cited in the passage.

Core Idea
Jihad is a communal obligation; children, slaves, women, and the disabled are exempt.

Jihad is not an individual duty for every Muslim. Rather, it is a communal obligation (fard kifayah). This passage from a Hanafi commentary clarifies the rule: if some perform it, the rest are absolved; if all abandon it, all sin. It also specifies who is not obligated—those who lack legal capacity or ability. Understanding these exemptions helps us apply the ruling correctly in different contexts.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of fard kifayah
The passage begins by explaining that if some undertake jihad, it falls from the rest. This is the classical definition: a communal obligation that, when fulfilled by a sufficient number, removes the sin from the whole community.
Note that fard kifayah is distinguished from fard 'ayn; the former becomes a personal obligation only if no one else performs it.
2
Identify the exempt categories
The passage lists six categories: child, slave, woman, blind, lame, and crippled. Each is exempt for a specific reason related to legal responsibility or physical ability.
The blind, lame, and crippled are also covered by the Quranic verse about 'those with harm'.
3
Analyze the reason for each exemption
For each exempt category, the commentary explains: child and insane lack taklif; slave has a master's right; woman has weak constitution or husband's right; physically disabled are excused by Quran.
Note that if the slave's master permits, or the woman's husband permits (or she is unmarried), the obligation may apply.
4
Examine the proofs from Quran and Hadith
The passage cites two Quranic verses (24:61 and 4:95) to exempt the blind, lame, and sick, and a hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari showing women accompanied to serve but were not obligated to fight.
These proofs are explicit in exempting certain groups, confirming that jihad is not obligatory on them.
5
Apply the ruling to new scenarios
Using the principles derived, you can determine whether individuals with similar conditions (e.g., chronic illness, severe disability) are exempt. The key is the presence of a genuine excuse that prevents participation.
In contemporary contexts, the exemptions are limited to genuine incapacity; mere preference or laziness does not exempt.

Source Text

إن قام به البعض سقط عن الباقين فإن تركوا أثموا إلا على صبي، وعبد، وامرأة، وأعمى، ومقعد، وأقطع. قوله : إن قام؛ هذه الجملة كالتفسير لفرض الكفاية. قوله : سقط؛ فيه إشارة إلى أن فرض الكفاية يكون فرضا على كل واحد، لكن يسقط عن الباقين بفعل بعضهم؛ لحصول المقصود، وتحقيقه في كتب الأصول. قوله : إلا على صبي ... الخ؛ عدم افتراضه على الصبي لكونه من غير المكلفين لا يخاطب بسائر الفرائض، ومثله المجنون، وعدمه على العبد لحق المولى، فإن حق العبد مقدم، فلو أذن له المولى افترض عليه، وعدمه على المرأة لكونها ليست من أهله لضعف بنيتها، وقيل: لحق الزوج. ومفاده الافتراض على غير المتزوجة، وعلى المتزوجة بإذن الزوج، والصحيح هو الوجه الأول، وقد ثبت في صحيح البخاري وغيره: أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا ذهب إلى الغزو ذهبت معه بعض النساء، فكن يخدمن المرضى ويداوين الجرحى، ولم يكن يلزم عليهن الذهاب معه، ولا القتال. وكذا أصحاب الأعذار والمرضى لا يفترض عليهم؛ لقوله: {لَيْسَ عَلَى الْأَعْمَى حَرَجٌ وَلَا عَلَى الْأَعْرَجِ حَرَجٌ وَلَا عَلَى الْمَرِيضِ حَرَجٌ}، وقوله: {لَا يَسْتَوِي الْقَاعِدُونَ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ غَيْرُ أُولِي الضَّرَرِ وَالْمُجَاهِدُونَ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ} الآية. قوله: ومقعد؛ على صيغة اسم المفعول، هو من أقعده الداء عن الحركة، وقيل: هو الزمن، وقيل: متشنج الأعضاء، وقيل: هو الأعرج، كذا في المغرب والفتح.
If some undertake it, it falls from the rest; if they abandon it, they are sinful, except for a child, a slave, a woman, a blind person, a lame person, and a crippled person. His statement: 'If some undertake it' – this sentence is an interpretation of fard kifayah. His statement: 'it falls' – indicates that fard kifayah is an obligation on each one, but falls from the rest by the action of some because the objective is achieved, and its verification is in the books of usul. His statement: 'except for a child...' – the obligation is not upon the child because he is not among the obligated; he is not addressed with the other obligations, similarly the insane. Its absence on the slave is due to the master's right, for the slave's right is given precedence; if the master permits him, it becomes obligatory upon him. Its absence on the woman is because she is not of its people due to her weak constitution; it is said: due to the husband's right. Its purport is that it becomes obligatory upon the unmarried woman and upon the married woman with her husband's permission; the correct is the first view. It is established in Sahih al-Bukhari and others that the Prophet, peace be upon him, when he went to battle, some women went with him, and they would serve the sick and treat the wounded, and he did not oblige them to go with him nor to fight. Similarly, those with excuses and the sick are not obliged upon them; due to His statement: {There is no blame upon the blind nor upon the lame nor upon the sick} and His statement: {Not equal are the sitting among the believers – other than those with harm – and the mujahideen in the cause of Allah} the verse. His statement: 'and a crippled person (muq'ad)' – on the pattern of the passive participle, it is one whom an illness has prevented from movement; it is said: the aged; and said: one with contracted limbs; and said: the lame; as in al-Mughrib and al-Fath.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on the matn where the author explains the ruling of jihad as fard kifayah. The matn states that if some people perform jihad, the obligation is removed from the rest; but if all abandon it, all are sinful. Then it excludes certain persons: child, slave, woman, blind, lame, and crippled. The commentary then explains the reason for each exclusion: the child is not mukallaf (legally responsible); the slave is bound by his master's right; the woman is not from the people of jihad due to weak constitution (or due to husband's right); the blind, lame, and sick are excused by Quranic verses. The commentary also quotes a hadith that women used to accompany the Prophet to serve the sick and wounded, not to fight. The discussion on 'muq'ada' (crippled) defines the term as one prevented from movement by illness.

Key Terms
فرض الكفاية (fard al-kifayah): A communal obligation; if performed by some, it is lifted from the rest; if abandoned by all, all sin.
صبي (sabi): A child who has not reached puberty, not legally obligated for any fard.
عبد ('abd): A slave; jihad is not obligatory upon him without his master's permission due to the master's right.
امرأة (imra'ah): A woman; exempt from jihad due to weak constitution or husband's right, though she may accompany for support roles.
مقعد (muq'ad): A crippled person, one prevented from movement by illness or deformity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) She is weak in faith.
B) Her weak constitution or the right of her husband.
C) She lacks bravery.
D) She is not permitted by the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Jihad is a communal obligation (fard kifayah), and those who lack legal capacity or physical ability are exempt.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules

Jihad as Fard 'Ayn in General Mobilization
Explains when jihad becomes individual obligation and who may participate without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that triggers jihad as fard 'ayn and identify which individuals may participate without permission.

Core Idea
Jihad becomes fard 'ayn when the enemy attacks and the objective cannot be achieved without all; permission from authority is then overridden.

Jihad is normally a collective obligation (fard kifayah), but when the enemy attacks a Muslim town, it becomes an individual duty (fard 'ayn) on every capable person. This lesson explains the rationale and the practical consequences, including who may go out without permission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the usual ruling of jihad
Start with the base ruling: jihad is normally fard kifayah, meaning if some perform it, others are absolved.
This is the default state.
2
Recognize the exception: enemy attack
When the enemy attacks a Muslim town (general mobilization), jihad becomes fard 'ayn. The objective – repelling evil – cannot be achieved by a few alone.
This is called al-nafir al-'amm.
3
Understand the rationale (the secret)
Jihad is prescribed not for itself but to defend faith and repel evil. If the goal is attainable by some, it remains fard kifayah; otherwise, it becomes fard 'ayn.
Reference to al-Sarakhsi's explanation.
4
Apply the ruling: who may go without permission
Since it is fard 'ayn, normal restrictions are lifted: a slave does not need his master's permission, a woman does not need her husband's permission, and a child (if able) does not need parents' permission.
Based on the hadith: 'No obedience to a creature in disobedience to the Creator.'
5
Note the evidence
The hadith (reported by al-Tirmidhi) establishes the principle that when an act is fard, one cannot be prevented by any authority.
This overrides all permissions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفرض عين إن هجموا، فتخرج المرأة، والعبد بلا إذن. قوله : وفرض عين؛ عطف على قوله : فرض كفاية، وحاصله : إن الجهاد يصير فرض عين إذا هجم العدو على بلدة من بلاد المسلمين وتسلطوا عليها، وهذه الحالة تسمى بالنفير العام. والسر في ذلك على ما في شرح السير الكبير للسرخسي وغيره : إن الجهاد لم يفرض الحسن في نفسه، فإنه في نفسه تعذيب عباد الله، وتخريب بلاد الله علة، وإنما فرض لإعلاء كلمة الله، ودفع الشر عن عباد الله، وكل ما فرض لغيره معه، يصير فرض كفاية إذا حصل المقصود بالبعض، وفرض عين إذا لم يحصل. ولذا كان النبي يخرج إلى الغزو، ولا يكلف كل من كان في المدينة للخروج ولا يلام المتخلف إلا في النفير العام، ففي صورة هجوم الكفار المقصود هو دفع شرهم، ولا يحصل بإقامة البعض، فيفترض على الكل افتراض عين، حتى يجب الخروج على العبد بدون إذن المولى، وعلى المرأة بدون إذن الزوج، والبالغ بدون إذن الوالدين، فإن أداء فرض غير محتاج إلى إذن عبد، فلا طاعة لمخلوق في معصية خالق، كما ورد به الحديث أخرجه الترمذي، بل يأثم من منع في هذه الصورة. قوله : والعبد بلا إذن؛ قال شمس الأئمة السرخسي : وكذلك الغلمان إذا أطاقوا القتال، فلا بأس بأن يخرجوا ويقاتلوا في النفير العام، وإن كره ذلك الآباء والأمهات. وذكر في «الفتح» وغيره : إنه يشترط للفرضية الاستطاعة على القتال والدفع، فمن قدر على الخروج دون الدفع ينبغي له أن يخرج تكثيراً للسواد وإرهاباً.
And it is fard 'ayn if they attack; then the woman and the slave go out without permission. His statement: 'and fard 'ayn' – it is conjuncted to his statement: 'fard kifayah', and its summary: jihad becomes fard 'ayn when the enemy attacks a town of the Muslims and overpowers them, and this situation is called general mobilization. The secret behind that, as in Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir by al-Sarakhsi and others: jihad was not prescribed for the good in itself, for in itself it is tormenting Allah's servants and destroying Allah's lands, but rather it was prescribed for the exaltation of Allah's word and repelling evil from His servants. Whatever is prescribed for something else, if the objective is achieved by some, it becomes fard kifayah; if not achieved, fard 'ayn. Hence the Prophet used to go out to battle and did not burden everyone in Madinah to go out, nor blame the one who stayed behind except in general mobilization. In the case of the attack of the disbelievers, the objective is to repel their evil, and that is not achieved by the action of some, so it becomes fard 'ayn on everyone, to the extent that a slave must go out without his master's permission, a woman without her husband's permission, and an adult without his parents' permission; for performing a fard does not need the permission of a servant, and there is no obedience to a creature in disobedience to the Creator, as the hadith reported by al-Tirmidhi states. Rather, the one who prevents is sinful in this situation. His statement: 'and the slave without permission'; Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: similarly, young boys who are able to fight – there is no harm in they going out and fighting in general mobilization, even if parents dislike that. It is mentioned in al-Fath and others: the condition for obligatory status is the ability to fight and repel; whoever is able to go out but not to repel should go out to increase the numbers and show force.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage explains the transition of jihad from fard kifayah to fard 'ayn in the case of a general enemy attack. The commentator emphasizes that jihad is not an end in itself but a means to defend religion and repel evil. Therefore, when the objective cannot be achieved by a few, it becomes obligatory on all capable individuals. Consequently, normal exemptions are lifted: a slave does not need his master's permission, a woman does not need her husband's permission, and a child (if able to fight) does not need his parents' permission. The commentator also adds that the ability to fight is a condition; those who cannot fight should still go out to swell the ranks.

Key Terms
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): An individual obligation; every capable person must perform it; cannot be fulfilled by others.
النفير العام (al-nafir al-'amm): General mobilization when the enemy attacks a Muslim town; jihad becomes fard 'ayn on all capable.
لا طاعة لمخلوق في معصية الخالق (la ta'ata li makhluqin fi ma'siyati al-khaliq): A principle: one must not obey any creature if that obedience leads to disobedience to the Creator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A slave needs his master's permission to fight.
C) A woman may go out to fight without her husband's permission.

Key Takeaway
General mobilization transforms jihad from a collective duty to an individual obligation, overriding usual permissions.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate

Jihad as Fard 'Ayn: Conditions for Individual Obligation
Expansion on the trigger and conditions for fard 'ayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which jihad becomes fard 'ayn and identify who is obligated without requiring permission.

Core Idea
Jihad becomes individually obligatory when enemies attack and repelling them requires everyone's effort—no master, husband, or parent can prevent you.

Jihad is normally a communal obligation, but this passage explains the critical exception: when enemies attack a Muslim territory, it transforms into an individual duty for all capable Muslims. This shift has profound implications for who must fight and whose permission is needed. Let's explore the reasoning and conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling and the exceptional case
State that jihad is normally fard kifayah (communal obligation). Identify the trigger for fard 'ayn (individual obligation): when enemies attack a Muslim town (nafir 'amm).
2
Understand the rationale for the transformation
Explain why jihad was prescribed: not for its own sake but to elevate Allah's word and repel evil. Since the objective (repelling the enemy) cannot be achieved by only some Muslims, it becomes obligatory on all.
3
Apply the consequence: permission is overridden
Recognize that when jihad becomes fard 'ayn, a slave, wife, or child may go out without permission from master, husband, or parents. The hadith 'No obedience to a creature in disobedience to the Creator' supports this.
4
Trace the geographical spread of obligation
The obligation first applies to those nearest the attacked frontier (thaghr). If they are insufficient, it spreads to those further away, potentially to all Muslims if the threat requires it.
5
Identify the condition of capability
Note that obligation is contingent on ability to fight (istita'ah): having weapons, provisions, and the strength to repel. Those who cannot fight but can go out to increase numbers are recommended to do so.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجهاد / حكمه وكيفيته
وفرض عين إن هجموا، فتخرج المرأة، والعبد بلا إذن
قوله : وفرض عين ؛ عطف على قوله : فرض كفاية، وحاصله : إنّ الجهاد يصير فرض عين إذا هجم العدوّ على بلدة من بلاد المسلمين وتسلّطوا عليها، وهذه الحالة تسمى بالنفير العام. والسر في ذلك على ما في شرح السير الكبير للسِّرَخْسِي ه وغيره : إِنَّ الجهاد لم يفرض الحسن في نفسه، فإنّه في نفسه تعذيب عبادِ الله ، وتخريب بلادِ الله علة ، وإنّما فُرِضَ لإعلاء كلمة الله ، ودفع الشر عن عباد الله ، وكل ما فرض لغيره يصير فرض كفاية إذا حصل المقصود بالبعض ، وفرض عين إذا لم يحصل. ولذا كان النبي يخرج إلى الغزو ، ولا يكلّف كل من كان في المدينة للخروج ولا يلام المتخلّف إلا في النفير العام، ففي صورة هجوم الكفّار المقصود هو دفعُ شرهم، ولا يحصل بإقامة البعض، فيفترض على الكل افتراض عين، حتى يجب الخروج على العبد بدون إذن المولى، وعلى المرأة بدون إذن الزوج، والبالغ بدون إذن الوالدين، فإنّ أداء فرض غير محتاج إلى إذن عبد ، فـلا طاعة لمخلوق في معصية خالق، كما ورد به الحديث أخرجه الترمذي، بل يأثمُ من منع في هذه الصورة. [قوله : والعبد بلا إذن] قال شمس الأئمة السَّرَخْسي : وكذلك الغلمان إذا أطاقوا القتال، فلا بأس بأن يخرجوا ويقاتلوا في النفير العام، وإن كره ذلك الآباء والأمهات. وذكر في «الفتح» وغيره : إنّه يشترط للفرضيّة الاستطاعة على القتال والدفع ، فمن قدر على الخروج دون الدفع ينبغي له أن يخرج تكثيراً للسواد وإرهاباً. فإنه إذا هجم الكفّار على ثغر من الثغور يصير فرض عين على من كان يقرب منه، وهم يقدرون على الجهاد. وأما على من وراءهم، فإذا بلغ الخبر إليهم يصير فرض عين عليهم إذا احتيج إليهم بأن خيف على من كان يقرب منهم، بأنهم عاجزون عن المقاومة، أو بأن لم يعجزوا، ولكن تكاسلوا، ثم إلى أن يصير فرض عين على جميع أهل الإسلام شرقاً وغرباً. قوله : على ثغر من الثغور - بضم الثاء المثلثة، بعدها غين معجمة – جمع ثغر – بالفتح - : هو موضع المخافة من العدو، ويطلق على الموضع الذي ليس وراءه تسلّط أهل الإسلام والإقامة في مثل هذا الموضع لدفع هجوم الكفار يسمّى رباطاً، وهو المراد بقوله : رباط يوم في سبيل الله خير من صيام شهر وقيامه، وإن مات فيه أجرى عليه عمله الذي كان يعمل، وأجرى عليه رزقه، وأمن الفتان) أخرجه مسلم. وفي الباب أخبار كثيرة مخرجة في كتب السنن وغيرها. قال في «البدائع»: «لا ينبغي للإمام أن يُخلي ثغراً من الثغور من جماعة من المسلمين فيهم غناء وكفاية لقتال العدوّ، فإن قاموا به سقط عن الباقين، وإن ضعف أهل ثغر عن مقاومة الكفرة، وخيف عليهم من العدو، فعلى من وراءهم من المسلمين الأقرب فالأقرب أن ينفروا إليهم، وأن يمدوهم بالسلاح والكراع والمال؛ لما ذكر أنه فرض على الناس كلّهم ممن هو من أهل الجهاد، ولكن سقط الفرضُ عنهم لحصول الكفاية بالبعض، فما لم يحصل لم يسقط». قوله : وهم يقدرون؛ أشار به إلى أنّ الفرضيّة منوطة بالقدرة على الجهاد، وهي بالقدرة على السلاح، وعلى الزاد والراحلة ونحو ذلك. قوله : يصير فرض عين عليهم؛ قال في «الفتح»: كان معناه إذا دام الحرب بقدر ما يصل الأبعدون ويبلغهم الخبر وإلا فهو تكليف ما لا يطاق.
Book of Jihad: Its Ruling and Its Modality. And it is an individual obligation if they (enemies) attack, so a woman and a slave go out without permission. His saying: 'And individual obligation' is a conjunction to his saying: 'communal obligation'. The summary: Jihad becomes an individual obligation when the enemy attacks a town among the Muslim towns and dominates it, and this situation is called general mobilization (al-nafir al-amm). The reason for this, according to what is in Sharh al-Siyar al-Kabir by al-Sarakhsi and others, is that jihad was not prescribed for its own sake, for in itself it is tormenting the servants of Allah and destroying the lands of Allah, but it was prescribed to elevate the word of Allah and to repel evil from the servants of Allah. Everything prescribed for something else becomes a communal obligation if the objective is achieved by some, and an individual obligation if it is not achieved. Therefore the Prophet (peace be upon him) would go out to battle and not oblige everyone in Medina to go out, nor would he blame those who stayed behind except in general mobilization. In the case of the attack of the disbelievers, the objective is to repel their evil, and it cannot be achieved by the effort of some, so it becomes obligatory upon all as an individual obligation, such that it is obligatory for a slave to go out without the permission of his master, for a woman without the permission of her husband, and for an adult without the permission of his parents, because performing an obligation does not require the permission of any servant, and there is no obedience to a creation in disobedience to the Creator, as reported in the hadith narrated by al-Tirmidhi. Rather, the one who prevents (them) in this situation is sinful. His saying: 'and the slave without permission' – Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: Likewise, young boys if they are able to fight, there is no harm if they go out and fight in general mobilization, even if their parents dislike it. It is mentioned in al-Fath and elsewhere: Capability for fighting and repelling is a condition for the obligation; so whoever can go out but cannot repel, it is recommended for him to go out to increase the numbers and to instill awe. For if the disbelievers attack a frontier post (thaghr) among the frontier posts, it becomes an individual obligation upon those who are near it and are able to fight. As for those behind them, when the news reaches them, it becomes an individual obligation upon them if they are needed, either because it is feared that those near are unable to resist, or they are not unable but are lazy; then [it spreads] until it becomes an individual obligation upon all Muslims east and west. His saying: 'upon a frontier post' – with damm on the tha, followed by a mu'jam ghayn – plural thughur (with fatha on tha) – it is a place of fear from the enemy, and it refers to a place beyond which there is no Muslim authority. Residing in such a place to repel the attack of the disbelievers is called ribat, and it is what is meant by his saying: 'A day of ribat in the path of Allah is better than a month of fasting and its night prayers; if he dies there, his deeds that he used to do will continue to be recorded for him, his provision will be continued, and he will be secure from the great terror' – reported by Muslim. There are many traditions on this chapter in the collections of Sunan and others. He said in al-Bada'i': 'It is not proper for the Imam to leave a frontier post empty of a group of Muslims who have sufficient strength and capability to fight the enemy. If they undertake it, it falls from the rest; but if the people of a frontier post are weak against the disbelievers and it is feared for them from the enemy, then upon those Muslims behind them – the nearest then the nearest – they must go forth to them and aid them with weapons, cavalry, and wealth, because it has been mentioned that it is an obligation upon all the people who are fit for jihad, but the obligation fell from them because sufficiency was achieved by some; so as long as it is not achieved, it does not fall.' His saying: 'and they are able' – he indicated by this that obligation is contingent upon ability to fight, which is ability regarding weapons, provisions, riding animals, and the like. His saying: 'it becomes an individual obligation upon them' – he said in al-Fath: Its meaning is if the war continues enough for the farthest ones to arrive and the news reaches them; otherwise it is an impossible obligation.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of when jihad, which is normally a communal obligation (fard kifayah), becomes an individual obligation (fard ayn). The commentator expands on the base text: "And it is an individual obligation if they attack, so a woman and a slave go out without permission." The key trigger is a general mobilization (nafir amm) when enemies attack a Muslim town. The underlying rationale, as stated by al-Sarakhsi, is that jihad is prescribed not for its own sake (since it involves destruction and hardship) but to elevate Allah's word and repel evil. When the objective of repelling the enemy cannot be achieved by some Muslims alone, it becomes obligatory on all capable individuals. This overrides normal permissions: a slave does not need his master's permission, a wife does not need her husband's permission, and an adult child does not need parents' permission. The hadith "No obedience to a creature in disobedience to the Creator" supports this. The obligation is conditional on capability (istita'ah) for fighting and repelling. If a person can only go out to increase numbers without being able to fight, it is recommended (not obligatory). The obligation spreads geographically: first on those nearest the attacked frontier post (thaghr), then on those further away when news reaches them if needed, and eventually on all Muslims worldwide if the danger is not contained. The passage also defines thaghr and ribat, citing the virtue of ribat. The commentator quotes from al-Bada'i' and al-Fath to clarify the obligation's spread and its limits (it cannot be an obligation if impossible).

Key Terms
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): An individual obligation: every capable Muslim must perform it; if some do it, it does not exempt others in this context because the objective cannot be achieved by a few.
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A communal obligation: if sufficient Muslims perform it, the obligation falls from the rest; but if none do, all sin.
نفير عام (nafir 'amm): General mobilization: when enemies attack a Muslim territory, all capable Muslims are called to arms; jihad becomes fard 'ayn.
ثغر (thaghr): A frontier post: a place near enemy territory where Muslims guard against attack. Plural: thughur.
رباط (ribat): Residing at a frontier post for the purpose of defending against the enemy; highly meritorious.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for jihad to become fard 'ayn (individual obligation) rather than fard kifayah?
A) When the Prophet (peace be upon him) personally calls for it
B) When enemies attack a Muslim town and the objective of repelling them cannot be achieved by some Muslims alone
C) When a ruler orders all Muslims to fight
D) When a Muslim has sufficient wealth

Key Takeaway
Jihad becomes an individual obligation for all capable Muslims when enemies attack a Muslim territory, overriding normal permissions, because repelling the threat requires everyone's effort.

The Gradual Obligation of Jihad: From Fard Kifayah to Fard 'Ayn
Establishes when jihad becomes fard 'ayn and spreads to others

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which jihad transitions from fard kifayah to fard 'ayn and apply the rule to a scenario involving successive Muslim communities.

Core Idea
Jihad becomes individually obligatory only when attackers threaten a border and the nearest defenders are incapable or negligent.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the Hanafi ruling on when jihad becomes an individual obligation (fard 'ayn). Normally jihad is a communal duty (fard kifayah), but when disbelievers attack a border town (thaghr), the obligation expands in stages: first on those nearby if capable, then on those farther away if needed, and ultimately on all Muslims if the attack persists and news spreads. The commentary also defines key terms like thaghr and ribat, and cites a hadith on the virtue of ribat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering event
Find the condition that changes jihad from fard kifayah to fard 'ayn: an enemy attack on a thaghr (border town).
Thaghr is defined as a place of vulnerability beyond which Muslim authority does not extend.
2
Determine the first obligation layer
The attack makes jihad fard 'ayn on those nearest the thaghr who are capable of fighting (able to provide weapons, provisions, mounts).
Capability is a necessary condition for any obligation.
3
Determine subsequent layers
If those nearest are unable or neglectful, the obligation spreads to the next nearest when news reaches them and they are needed.
The spread continues until it becomes fard 'ayn on all Muslims if the attack persists and news circulates.
4
Understand the role of capability
The obligation is contingent on capability (weapons, provisions, mounts). Those who lack the means are not obligated.
This prevents hardship.
5
Apply the analogy with funeral prayer
The commentator compares the spread of obligation to funeral prayer: initially on neighbors, then on others if the nearer neglect it.
This clarifies the graduated nature of the duty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإنه إذا هجم الكفّار على ثغر من الثغور يصير فرض عين على من كان يقرب منه، وهم يقدرون على الجهاد. وأما على من وراءهم، فإذا بلغ الخبر إليهم يصير فرض عين عليهم إذا احتيج إليهم بأن خيف على من كان يقرب منهم، بأنهم عاجزون عن المقاومة ، أو بأن لم يعجزوا ، ولكن تكاسلوا، ثُمَّ  َوثُمَّ إلى أن يصير فرض عين على جميع أهل الإسلام شرقاً وغرباً. [1]قوله : على ثغر من الثغور ؛ - بضم الثاء المثلثة، بعدها غين معجمة – ، جمع ثغر – بالفتح - : هو موضعُ المخافة من العدو، ويطلق على الموضع الذي ليس وراءه تسلّط أهل الإسلام والإقامة في مثل هذا الموضع لدفع هجوم الكفار يسمّى رباطاً ، وهو المراد بقوله : رباط يوم في سبيل الله خير من صيام شهر وقيامه، وإن مات فيه أجرى عليه عمله الذي كان يعمل، وأجرى عليه رزقه ، وأمن الفتان) ، أخرجه مسلم ، وفي الباب أخبار كثيرة مخرجة في كتب السنن وغيرها. (٢) قوله : على من كان...الخ ؛ قال في «البدائع»: «لا ينبغي للإمام أن يُخلّي ثغراً من الثغور من جماعة من المسلمين فيهم غناء وكفاية لقتال العدوّ ، فإن قاموا به، عن الباقين، وإن ضعف أهل ثغر عن مقاومة الكفرة، وخيف عليهم من العدو. فعلى من وراءهم من المسلمين الأقرب فالأقرب أن ينفروا إليهم، وأن يمدوهم بالسلاح والكراع والمال ؛ لما ذكر أنه فرض على الناس كلّهم ممن هو من أهل الجهاد، ولكن سقط الفرضُ عنهم لحصول الكفاية بالبعض ، فما لم يحصل لم يسقط». [٣] قوله : وهم يقدرون ؛ أشار به إلى أنّ الفرضيّة منوطة بالقدرة على الجهاد، وهي بالقدرة على السلاح، وعلى الزاد والراحلة ونحو ذلك. [٤] قوله : يصير فرض عين عليهم ؛ قال في «الفتح» " : كان معناه إذا دام الحرب بقدر ما يصل الأبعدون ويبلغهم الخبر وإلا فهو تكليف ما لا يطاق. وهذا نظير صلاة الجنازة تصيرُ فرضاً على جيرانه دون من هو بعيد عن الميت، فإن قام بها الأقربون، أو بعضهم سقط عن الكل، وإن بلغ إلى الأبعد أن الأقربين ضيعوا حقه ، فعلى الأبعد أن يقوم بها ، فإن ترك الكل، فكلُّ مَن بلغ إليه خبر موته يصير آثماً.
For if the disbelievers attack a border town, it becomes an individual obligation upon those who are near it, and they are capable of jihad. As for those behind them, when the news reaches them, it becomes an individual obligation upon them if they are needed, either because it is feared for those near them due to their inability to resist, or because they are not unable but are negligent. Then successively, until it becomes an individual obligation upon all Muslims, east and west. [1] His saying: 'upon a border town (thaghr)' – with a damma on the tha and a mu'jamah ghayn, plural of thaghr (with fatha): it is a place of fear from the enemy, and it is said of a place beyond which the authority of Islam does not extend. Residing in such a place to repel the attack of disbelievers is called ribat, and it is referred to in his saying: 'A day of ribat in the path of Allah is better than a month of fasting and night prayer, and if he dies there, his deeds that he used to do continue to be recorded, his provision continues, and he is protected from the trial (of the grave).' Narrated by Muslim. There are many other hadith on this topic in the books of Sunan etc. (2) His saying: 'upon those who are...' etc. Al-Bada'i' says: 'It is not fitting for the Imam to leave any border town without a group of Muslims who have sufficient strength and capability to fight the enemy. If they undertake it, it suffices for the rest. If the people of a border town are weak against the disbelievers and it is feared for them from the enemy, then those behind them, the nearest then the nearest, must rush to them and supply them with weapons, mounts, and wealth, because jihad has been mentioned as an obligation upon all who are capable, but it fell due to sufficiency by some. When sufficiency is not achieved, it does not fall.' [3] His saying: 'and they are capable' indicates that the obligation is contingent on capability for jihad, which is capability of weapons, provisions, and mounts, etc. [4] His saying: 'it becomes an individual obligation upon them' – Al-Fath says: 'Its meaning is if the war continues long enough for those farther away to arrive and the news reaches them, otherwise it is an obligation beyond capacity.' This is analogous to the funeral prayer: it becomes an obligation upon the neighbors, not on those far from the deceased. If the nearest, or some of them, perform it, it falls from all. If it reaches the more distant that the nearer have neglected their duty, then the more distant must perform it. If all abandon it, then everyone to whom news of the death reaches becomes sinful.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the ruling that jihad becomes fard 'ayn (individual obligation) when disbelievers attack a border town. The commentator first defines 'thaghr' as a place of vulnerability to enemy attack, and explains that residing there for defense is called 'ribat', citing a hadith from Muslim about its great reward. He then quotes Al-Bada'i' to explain that the Imam must station capable Muslims at borders; if they suffice, the obligation falls from others, but if they are weak, the nearest Muslims must rush to aid with weapons, mounts, and wealth. The obligation becomes fard 'ayn only on those capable—having arms, provisions, etc. The commentator further clarifies that if the war continues long enough for distant Muslims to hear the news, they too become obligated; otherwise, it is not required. He draws an analogy with funeral prayer: initially it is fard kifayah on the neighbors, but if they neglect it, it becomes fard 'ayn on those further away if news reaches them, and all who hear become sinful if it is left undone.

Key Terms
ثغر (thaghr): A border town or place vulnerable to enemy attack, beyond which Muslim authority does not extend.
رباط (ribat): Residing in a border town for the purpose of defending against enemy attack.
فرض عين (fard 'ayn): An individual obligation that must be performed by every capable person, unlike fard kifayah which is communal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does jihad become fard 'ayn on Muslims distant from the attacked border?
A) Immediately upon the attack, regardless of distance.
B) Only if the nearest Muslims are incapable or neglectful, and news reaches them.
C) Only if the Imam issues a general call.
D) Never, since jihad is always fard kifayah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that jihad becomes individually obligatory in stages, contingent on attack, capability, and spread of news.

Ruling on Ja'l (Forced Levy) for Jihad
States the ruling on imposing a levy on people for jihad when treasury has funds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the Imam imposing a forced levy (ja'l) for jihad and identify the condition that determines its permissibility or dislike.

Core Idea
A forced levy for jihad is disliked when the treasury suffices, but permissible when it does not.

This lesson addresses a practical matter of public finance and jihad: may the Imam compel people to contribute funds or supplies to support the army when the public treasury already has sufficient resources? The Hanafi school, based on the example of the Prophet ﷺ and the principle of avoiding unjust imposition, distinguishes between situations of treasury sufficiency and insufficiency. We will unpack the ruling, its evidence, and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Define ja'l and its application
Understand that ja'l here means a forced levy imposed by the Imam on the people to equip the mujahideen, not a voluntary charity or contractual wage. The term is defined in the text as 'what is given to a person in return for something he does.' In this context, it refers to compelling contributions of mounts, weapons, and provisions.
Ja'l differs from ijarah (hire) in that it is for a result, not for time or labour, and its permissibility is conditioned by necessity.
2
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two distinct situations: when the public treasury (bayt al-mal) has sufficient funds (from fay', ghanimah, or other sources) and when it does not. The ruling depends entirely on this condition.
Fay' here includes all treasury income, not just the narrow technical sense.
3
State the ruling for each scenario
When the treasury is sufficient: imposing a ja'l is makruh (disliked). When the treasury is insufficient: it is not disliked and is permissible (ja'iz). The text explicitly says 'and if there is none, then it is not disliked.'
The dislike is karahah tanzihiyyah according to some, but the text uses the term 'kariha' which can imply tahrimi; given the reasoning (resembles wage, no need), it is likely makruh tahrimi when unnecessary.
4
Examine the evidence
The primary evidence for the permissibility in the second scenario is the Prophet's action in the Tabuk expedition (Ghazwat al-Usrah), where he urged people to contribute when the treasury was insufficient. For the dislike in the first scenario, the reasoning is based on the principle that the treasury exists for such needs, so forcing contributions is unjust and resembles a wage without necessity.
The Quranic verse on cooperation in righteousness supports voluntary giving, but the ruling on compulsion derives from the Prophetic precedent and qiyas.
5
Consider voluntary contributions
The passage stresses that if people give willingly, without compulsion, it is permissible and even commendable, citing the Quranic command to cooperate in righteousness (al-Ma'idah 5:2). The dislike applies only when the Imam forces the levy without consent.
Thus, voluntary fundraising for jihad is always allowed, regardless of treasury status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكره الجعل مع فيء وبدونه لا : الجعلُ ما يجعلُ للعامل على عمله، والمراد أنه إذا كان في بيت المال شيءٌ لا يجعلُ الإمام على أرباب الأموال شيئاً من غير طيب أنفسهم ؛ ليتقوى به الغزاة ، أما إذا لم يكن فيه شيء، فيفعل ذلك. [1] قوله : وكره الجعل ؛ - بضم الجيم - ، ما يجعل للإنسان في مقابلة شيء يفعله، والمراد هاهنا أن يكلّف الإمامُ الناس بأن يقوّي بعضهم بعضاً بالكراع ؛ أي الخيل والسلاح وغير ذلك من النفقة والزاد ، كذا في «النهر»، ووجه الكراهة : أنه يشبه الأجر ولا ضرورة إليه ؛ لأنّ مالَ بيت المال معد لنوائب المسلمين. [٢] قوله : مع فيء ؛ – هو – بالفتح - كشيء، عبارة عمّا يؤخذ بغير قتال، كالخراج والجزية، والمأخوذ بقتال يسمّى غنيمة، والمراد بالفيء هاهنا ما يعم الغنيمة وغيرها كما أشار إليه الشارح ، فإنّ كراهة الجعل لا يختص بوجودِ الفيء المقابل للغنيمة فقط. بل تناط بوجودِ ما يكفي في بيت المال غنيمة كان أو فيئاً أو غير ذلك. [٣] قوله : وبدونه ؛ يعني إذا لم يكن في بيت المال كفاية لا يكره الجعل، بل للإمام أن يحرّض الناس على أن يقوّي بعضهم بعضاً، كما ثبت عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في غزوة تبوك ، وهي المعروفة بجيش العسرة. [٤] قوله : من غير طيب أنفسهم ؛ أي من غير رضاهم، فإن أعانوا بطيب النفس فلا بأس به ؛ لقوله : وَتَعَاوَنُوا عَلَى الْبِرِّ وَالتَّقْوَى . [٥] قوله : أما إذا لم يكن فيه شيء ؛ أي بقدر ما يكفي لتجهيز الجيوش.
And it is disliked to impose a ja'l (payment) when there is fay' (booty taken without fighting), and if there is none, it is not disliked. Al-ja'l is what is given to a worker for his work. The meaning is that if there is something in the public treasury, the Imam should not impose anything upon the owners of wealth without their consent, to strengthen the warriors. If there is nothing in it, then he may do that. [1] His saying: 'and it is disliked to impose a ja'l' – with a damma on the jim – it is what is given to a person in return for something he does. The meaning here is that the Imam charges people to support one another with al-kurā‘ (mounts), i.e., horses, weapons, and other expenses and provisions. So in 'Al-Nahr', and the reason for dislike is that it resembles a wage and there is no need for it because the treasury's property is prepared for the calamities of Muslims. [2] His saying: 'with fay' – with a fatha, like shay' – is an expression for what is taken without fighting, such as kharaj and jizya, and what is taken with fighting is called ghanimah. The meaning of fay' here is that which includes ghanimah and other things, as the commentator indicated. For the dislike of ja'l is not specific to the existence of fay' as opposed to ghanimah only, but rather it is dependent on the existence of what suffices in the treasury, whether it is ghanimah or fay' or something else. [3] His saying: 'and if there is none' means if the treasury does not have sufficient, then ja'l is not disliked. Rather, the Imam may urge people to support one another, as is established from the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the Tabuk expedition, known as the Army of Hardship. [4] His saying: 'without their consent' means without their pleasure. If they help willingly, then there is no harm, because of His saying: 'Cooperate in righteousness and piety' (Quran 5:2). [5] His saying: 'If there is nothing in it' means enough to equip the armies.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that it is makruh (disliked) for the Imam to impose a 'ja'l' (a forced levy or contribution) on the people to support the mujahideen when the public treasury (bayt al-mal) already has sufficient funds from fay' (non-war booty like kharaj and jizya) or ghanimah (war booty). The commentator explains that 'ja'l' is a payment given for work, and here it means the Imam compelling people to provide mounts, weapons, supplies, etc. The reason for dislike is that it resembles a wage and is unnecessary since the treasury is meant for such needs. If the treasury lacks funds, there is no dislike, and the Imam can urge people to contribute voluntarily, as the Prophet did in the Tabuk expedition (the Ghazwat al-Usrah). The commentator stresses that the dislike depends on the treasury having enough; it is not restricted to fay' specifically but to any sufficient funds. Additionally, if people give willingly, it is permissible. The Quranic verse on cooperation in righteousness supports voluntary contributions.

Key Terms
جعل (ja'l): A payment or compensation given to a person for something they do; here, a forced levy imposed by the Imam on people to support jihad.
فيء (fay'): Property taken from non-Muslims without fighting, such as kharaj (land tax) and jizya (poll tax), including ghanimah in a broader sense in this context.
بيت المال (bayt al-mal): The public treasury of the Muslims, which is used for the needs of the community, including equipping armies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it permissible (not disliked) for the Imam to impose a ja'l (forced levy) upon the people for jihad?
A) When the treasury has enough fay' but not ghanimah.
B) When the treasury does not have sufficient funds to equip the army.
C) It is always permissible regardless of treasury funds.
D) It is never permissible because it resembles wages.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on forced levies for jihad hinges on the sufficiency of the public treasury: sufficient treasury makes the levy disliked; insufficient treasury makes it permissible.

Ruling on Making Compensation (Ja'l) for Fighters from the Treasury
States ruling on ja'l with analogy to janazah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on imposing compensation (ja'l) on taxpayers to support fighters, and identify the conditions that determine its permissibility.

Core Idea
Ja'l is disliked when the treasury is sufficient, but permissible when insufficient, with consent.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah addresses a practical question of financing military campaigns: can the ruler compel taxpayers to contribute funds when the treasury is already adequate? The Hanafi answer is nuanced, balancing the collective obligation of jihad with the rights of individuals to consent to taxation. The ruling is tied to the state of the treasury and voluntary participation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its key terms
Understand what 'ja'l' means and the context: the ruler imposing a contribution on taxpayers to equip fighters. The passage distinguishes between two scenarios: with sufficient treasury funds (fei') and without.
Fei' here broadly includes all treasury income, not just non-war spoils.
2
State the ruling
The base ruling: with sufficient treasury, ja'l is makruh (disliked). Without sufficient treasury, it is not makruh.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah with no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf reported.
3
Understand the rationale
The dislike is because it resembles a wage (ujr) and there is no necessity when the treasury can cover costs. The treasury exists for public needs.
The commentary from Al-Nahr explains the reason.
4
Examine the analogy with janazah prayer
The author compares ja'l to the obligation of funeral prayer (fard kifayah). If the close neighbours perform it, it drops from others. Similarly, if the treasury covers needs, no extra burden is required.
This analogy helps clarify when a communal obligation can be transferred.
5
Identify the evidence and conditions
The Quranic verse (5:2) on cooperation in righteousness supports voluntary contributions. The condition for dislike is the sufficiency of the treasury; the condition for permissibility is insufficiency and consent.
Coercion without consent is disliked; voluntary aid is encouraged.

Book of Jihad: Its ruling and its manner. And making compensation (ja'l) along with fei' is disliked, and without it is not disliked. This is similar to the funeral prayer: it becomes obligatory upon the neighbors and not upon those far from the deceased. If the close ones perform it, or some of them, it falls from all. If it reaches the distant one that the close ones neglected his right, then the distant one must perform it. If all abandon it, then everyone who learns of his death becomes sinful. [4] And making compensation along with fei' and without it no: al-ja'l is what is given to the worker for his work. The meaning is that if there is something in the treasury, the ruler should not impose upon the people (taxpayers) anything without their consent to strengthen the fighters thereby. But if there is nothing in it, he may do that. [1] His statement: 'they neglected his right' means that they did not attend to his preparation and prayer upon him. [2] His statement: 'And making compensation is disliked' - with damma on the jim - it is what is given to a person in exchange for something he does. The meaning here is that the ruler imposes upon the people that they should strengthen one another by means of horses, weapons, and other expenses and provisions. This is from al-Nahr. The reason for dislike is that it resembles a wage and there is no need for it because the treasury wealth is prepared for the calamities of the Muslims. [3] His statement: 'along with fei'' - fei' is with fatha, like shay', the expression for what is taken without fighting, like kharaj and jizya. What is taken with fighting is called ghanima. The meaning of fei' here includes ghanima and other things as the commentator indicated. For the dislike of compensation is not specific to the existence of fei' as opposed to ghanima only, but rather it depends on the existence of sufficient funds in the treasury, whether it is ghanima, fei', or other. [4] His statement: 'and without it' means if there is not sufficient in the treasury, the compensation is not disliked; rather the ruler may incite the people to strengthen one another, as is established from the Prophet ﷺ in the expedition of Tabuk, which is known as the army of difficulty. [0] His statement: 'without their consent' means without their satisfaction. If they aid with satisfaction, there is no harm, due to His statement: 'And cooperate in righteousness and piety' (Quran 5:2). [6] His statement: 'but if there is nothing in it' means enough to equip the armies. (1) Al-Ma'idah: from verse 2.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah deals with the ruling of 'al-ja'l' (compensation or inducement) given to fighters from the state treasury (bayt al-mal). The ruling is stated: it is makruh (disliked) to impose such compensation upon the taxpayers when the treasury has sufficient funds, because it resembles a wage and there is no need, and the treasury is meant for public needs. However, if the treasury is insufficient, the ruler may incite people to voluntarily contribute, as the Prophet ﷺ did in the expedition of Tabuk. The passage also draws an analogy with the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah): it is a communal obligation (fard kifayah) that falls upon those near the deceased; if some fulfill it, it drops from others, but if all neglect it, all are sinful. Similarly, if the treasury lacks funds, the ruler may request contributions, but coercion without consent is disliked. The key condition is the state of the treasury and the willingness of the people. The Quranic verse (5:2) on cooperation in righteousness supports voluntary aid. The term 'fei'' here is used broadly to include all state income (ghanima, kharaj, jizya). This is a ruling from the Hanafi school, based on the principle of necessity and public interest.

Key Terms
الجعل (al-ja'l): Compensation or reward given to a person for performing a task; here, it refers to money or goods given to fighters from the treasury or collected from the people to support military campaigns.
فيء (al-fay'): Property taken from non-Muslims without fighting, such as kharaj (land tax) and jizya (poll tax); contrasted with ghanima (spoils taken by force). In this text, fay' is used broadly to include all state revenue.
بيت المال (bayt al-mal): The public treasury of the Islamic state, containing funds from various sources (zakah, fay', ghanima, etc.) intended for the welfare of Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it disliked (makruh) for the ruler to impose compensation (ja'l) on the taxpayers to support fighters?
A) When the treasury has sufficient funds
B) When the treasury is empty
C) When the taxpayers volunteer willingly
D) When the fighters are not in need

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on ja'l balances state necessity and individual consent: it is disliked when the treasury is sufficient, but permissible when it is lacking, provided consent is obtained.

Calling Enemies to Islam and Jizya Before Fighting
Ruling on the procedure of calling enemies to Islam and jizya during siege

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for calling enemies to Islam and jizya before combat, identify the hadith proofs, and explain why the Hanafi school classifies this as sunnah muakkadah.

Core Idea
The call to Islam must precede fighting; it is a confirmed sunnah, not a legal condition.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the proper procedure when besieging non-Muslims. The passage establishes that the invitation to Islam, and then to jizya, is a necessary precondition for combat, supported by explicit hadith and the practice of Salman al-Farsi. Understanding this ruling clarifies the ethical framework of jihad in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is calling the besieged enemies to Islam before fighting. Determine its legal status (wajib, sunnah, etc.) according to the Hanafi school.
The passage states that the Prophet never fought without calling, indicating a confirmed sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith proofs cited: the general hadith 'what qatala...', the specific command to Farwah, and the action of Salman al-Farsi.
These are ahad hadith, so thubut is zanni, but dalala is qati.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling. The negation of fighting until the call indicates that the call is a necessary precondition.
The imperative in the hadith could imply wujub, but Hanafi usul interprets it as nadb due to other evidence.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'i) consider the call wajib. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a confirmed sunnah and an obligation.
The practical difference: if the call is omitted, the Hanafi school deems the attack valid but the commander misses an emphasized sunnah.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in the Hanafi view, neglecting the call does not invalidate the combat, while in the Shafi'i view it might be sinful.
The Hanafi position is based on usul principles regarding the interpretation of commands.

Source Text

باب في كيفية القتال
(فإن حوصروا) : أي الكفار بأن حاصرهم المسلمون، (دعوا إلى الإسلام، فإن أبو ، فإلى الجزية ، فإن قبلوا، فلهم ما لنا، وعليهم ما علينا)
[1] قوله : دعوا إلى الإسلام ؛ أي يدعوهم الإمام ومن معه إلى الإسلام، فإن أسلموا فذلك هو الثابت من فعل الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وقوله : ففي «مستدرك الحاكم» و«مصنف عبد الرزاق» و«معجم الطبراني» و «مسند أحمد»: «ما قاتل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قوماً حتى دعاهم إلى الإسلام) وفي مسند أحمد عن فروة ، قال : أتيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقلت : أقاتل لمقبل قومي ومدبرهم، قال: نعم، فلمّا وليت دعاني فقال : لا تقاتلهم حتى تدعوهم إلى الإسلام». وعند أحمد والحاكم عن سلمان الفارسي : أنه انتهى إلى حصن أو مدينة ، فقال لأصحابه : دعوني أدعوهم كما رأيتُ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يدعوهم، فقال لهم : إنما كنت رجلاً منكم ، فهداني الله للإسلام، فإن أسلمتم فلكم ما لنا، وعليكم ما علينا، وإن أبيتم فأدوا الجزية وأنتم صاغرون، فإن أبيتهم فإنا ننبذ إليكم على سواء، إن الله له لا يحب الخائنين ، ففعل ذلك ثلاثة أيام، فلمّا كان اليوم الرابع أمر الناس فغزو إليها ففتحوها. [٢] قوله : فإلى الجزية ؛ أي دعوا إلى الجزية بأن يؤدّوها ويصيروا مطيعين لأهل الإسلام.
Chapter on the manner of fighting. (If they are besieged): i.e., the disbelievers, by the Muslims besieging them, (they are called to Islam; if they refuse, then to the jizya; if they accept, then for them is what is for us, and upon them is what is upon us). [1] His saying: they are called to Islam; meaning the Imam and those with him call them to Islam; if they become Muslim, that is what is established from the action of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). His saying: In Mustadrak al-Hakim, Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Mu'jam al-Tabarani, and Musnad Ahmad: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) never fought a people until he called them to Islam.' And in Musnad Ahmad from Farwah: He said: 'I came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said: Should I fight those who advance and those who retreat of my people? He said: Yes. Then when I turned away, he called me and said: Do not fight them until you call them to Islam.' And from Ahmad and al-Hakim from Salman al-Farsi: That he reached a fort or city and said to his companions: 'Let me call them as I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) calling them.' He said to them: 'I was only a man from among you, then Allah guided me to Islam. If you accept Islam, then for you is what is for us and upon you what is upon us. If you refuse, then pay the jizya while you are humiliated. If you refuse, then we will throw [the declaration of war] to you equally. Indeed, Allah does not love the treacherous.' He did that for three days. When it was the fourth day, he commanded the people to attack it, and they conquered it. [2] His saying: 'then to the jizya'; meaning they are called to the jizya by paying it and becoming obedient to the people of Islam.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school on the proper procedure when Muslims besiege non-Muslims. The author states that the besieged should first be called to embrace Islam. If they accept, they become full members of the Islamic state with identical rights and obligations as Muslims. If they refuse, they are then called to accept the jizya – a tax in exchange for protection and exemption from military service. Acceptance of jizya also gives them the same rights as Muslims in terms of protection and obligations in upholding the law. The commentator supports this ruling with multiple hadith proofs. The first is a general Prophetic practice: he never fought a people without first inviting them to Islam. The second hadith from Farwah explicitly commands: 'Do not fight them until you call them to Islam.' Finally, the story of Salman al-Farsi illustrates the procedure in action: he gave the call for three days before attacking. This indicates that the call is a necessary precondition for combat, and that the option of jizya follows only after rejection of Islam. The commentator clarifies that 'then to the jizya' means they are invited to pay the jizya and submit to Islamic authority. The Hanafi school holds that this calling is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) based on the consistent practice of the Prophet and his companions. It is not merely recommended but an integral part of the ethics of war in Islam.

Key Terms
الجزية (al-jizyah): A tax imposed on non-Muslims (dhimmis) in an Islamic state in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
صاغرون (sāghirūn): Humiliated; a condition of paying jizya indicating the submissive status of non-Muslims under Islamic rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Attack immediately
B) Call them to pay jizya
C) Call them to Islam
D) Offer them a truce

Key Takeaway
The call to Islam and jizya must precede fighting; this is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) based on the Prophet's practice and explicit hadith.

The Obligation to Call to Islam Before Fighting
Ruling with proof: obligation to invite before combat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that calling non-Muslims to Islam before fighting is wajib and identify the primary hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Fighting without prior invitation to Islam is impermissible — the call is wajib.

In the Hanafi school, the conduct of war is governed by strict ethical rules. This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah addresses a fundamental question: when Muslims besiege a non-Muslim population, what must happen before the first arrow is shot? The clear answer from the Prophet's practice is a sequential invitation: first to Islam, then to jizya, and only then, if both are refused, to war. Understanding this sequence is critical for the correct application of jihad in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The text states that when non-Muslims are besieged, they are 'called to Islam' (دعوا إلى الإسلام). The ruling is that this call is wajib (obligatory) before any fighting.
The Hanafi position is that this call is a condition for legitimate combat.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary cites multiple hadith, including a key report: 'The Messenger of God never fought a people until he called them to Islam' (ما قاتل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قوماً حتى دعاهم إلى الإسلام). This hadith is the primary proof.
The hadith is narrated in Mustadrak al-Hakim, Musnad Ahmad, and other collections.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove obligation? The phrase 'حتى دعاهم' (until he called them) indicates that calling was the boundary before fighting. In Hanafi usul, a link between two actions with 'حتى' implies a condition. Since the Prophet consistently did this, it establishes a wajib (binding) practice.
The evidence is zanni al-thubut (ahad hadith) but qati al-dalala in its meaning.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers this call to be sunnah (recommended), not wajib. They argue that the Prophet's general command to fight (e.g., 'I have been commanded to fight people until they say La ilaha illa Allah') does not require a separate call.
This difference has practical implications: a Shafi'i may engage immediately if the enemy is aware of Islam.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position relies on the explicit precedent and the command in the hadith of Salman al-Farisi, where the Prophet instructed him to call even before attacking a fortress. The weight of the evidence supports obligation.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi view: calling is wajib.

Source Text
