The Imam's Option to Leave Conquered Land with Its People and Impose Kharaj
Explains the imam's option to either divide booty or leave land with its people, with proof from Umar's decision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's option regarding conquered land and explain the proof from Umar's decision and Quranic verses.

Core Idea
The imam may leave conquered land with its people and impose kharaj, as Umar did, to benefit all Muslims.

This lesson examines the second option available to the imam upon conquering a territory by force: leaving the land with its original inhabitants and imposing kharaj and jizya. We will see how Umar (RA) applied this option in Iraq and how he used Quranic verses from Surah al-Hashr to justify it over dividing the land as booty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that the imam has the choice (ikhtiyar) between dividing the conquered land as booty among the army or leaving it with its people and imposing kharaj and jizya. This is the ruling of mubah (permissible).
Note that this applies only to lands conquered by force (anwatan).
2
Analyze the practice of Umar
The text cites the historical precedent of Umar (RA) who, when Iraq was conquered, chose to leave the land with its inhabitants and impose kharaj. This practice is recorded in Ibn Sa'd's Tabaqat.
Umar's decision is a key evidence for this ruling.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence from Abu Yusuf's Kitab al-Kharaj
Umar recited verses 59:7-10 which specify the recipients of fay': Allah, the Messenger, relatives, orphans, needy, wayfarer, and then the Muhajirun, Ansar, and those who come after them. He argued that dividing the land would deprive later generations.
The verses establish that fay' is for all Muslims, including future generations.
4
Understand the reasoning (maslahah)
The underlying principle is public interest (maslahah): keeping the land as a permanent source of revenue benefits the entire Muslim community perpetually.
This reasoning is used to support the option of leaving the land.
5
Note the practical consequence
If the imam divides the land, later Muslims receive no share. By leaving it and imposing kharaj, the revenue continues for all.
The mufta bihi is that the imam has this option, with Umar's precedent as the preferred practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو أقر أهله عليه

[1] قوله : أو أقرّ ؛ يعني الإمامُ بالخيار في المفتوح عنوة بين أن يقسمه على الجيش وبين أن يقر أهل ذلك المقام عليه، ويوظف عليهم جزية وخراجاً، هكذا فعله عمر الله حين فتح بلاد العراق، أخرجه ابن سعد في «الطبقات».

وفي كتاب «الخراج» للإمام أبي يوسف الله : «أما الفيء يا أمير المؤمنين فهو الخراج عندنا خراج الأرض ؛ لأنّ الله له يقول في كتابه : ما أَفَاءَ اللَّهُ عَلَى رَسُولِهِ مِنْ أَهْلِ القرى فَلِلَّهِ وَالرَّسُولِ وَلِذِي الْقُرْبَى وَالْيَتَى وَالْمَسَكِينِ وَابْنِ السَّبِيلِ كَى لَا يَكُونَ دُولَةٌ بَيْنَ الْأَغْنِيَاءِ منكم (١) إلى أن قال : لِلْفُقَرَاءِ الْمُهَاجِرِينَ الَّذِينَ أُخْرِجُوا مِن دِيَارِهِمْ وَأَمْوَالِهِمْ يَبْتَغُونَ فَضْلًا مِّنَ اللَّهِ وَرِضْوَانَا ) ثم قال جل ذكره : ﴿ وَالَّذِينَ تَبَوَّهُو الدَّارَ وَالإِيمَنَ مِن قَبْلِهِمْ يُحِبُّونَ مَنْ هَاجَرَ التهم (۳) ، وهذا فيما بلغنا في الأنصار خاصة، ثمّ قال له : وَالَّذِينَ جَاءُو مِنْ بعْدِهِمْ يَقُولُونَ رَبَّنَا اغْفِرْ لَنَا وَلا خَوَانِنَا الَّذِينَ سَبَقُونَا بِالإِيمَنِ (1)

فهذا والله أعلم لمن جاءَ بعدهم من المؤمنين إلى يوم القيامة، وقد سأل بلال وأصحابه عمر بن الخطاب له قسمة ما أفاء الله له عليهم من العراق والشام، وقالوا : قسموا الأرضين بين الذين افتتحوها كما تقسّم غنيمة العساكر، فأبي عمر ه ذلك وتلى عليهم هذه الآيات، وقال : قد أشرك الله له الذين يأتون من بعدكم في هذا الفيء، فلو قسمته لم يبق لمن بعدكم شيء.

قال أبو يوسف : حدثني بعض أشياخي عن يزيد بن حبيب : «إنَّ عمر ه كتب إلى سعد حين افتتح العراق ، أما بعد ؛ فقد بلغني كتابك تذكر فيه أنّ الناس سألوك أن تقسّم بينهم مغانمهم وما أفاء الله ، فإذا أتاك كتابي هذا فانظر ما أجلب الناسُ به عليك إلى العسكر من كراع أو مال ،
Or to leave its people upon it

[1] His statement: "or to leave" means the imam has the choice in what is conquered by force between dividing it among the army and leaving the people of that place upon it, and imposing upon them jizya and kharaj. This is what Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) did when he conquered the land of Iraq, as recorded by Ibn Sa'd in al-Tabaqat.

And in the Book of Kharaj by Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah be pleased with him): "As for the fay', O Commander of the Faithful, it is the kharaj according to us, the kharaj of the land, because Allah the Exalted says in His Book: 'What Allah has returned to His Messenger from the people of the towns belongs to Allah and the Messenger and to the near of kin and the orphans and the needy and the wayfarer, so that it may not circulate among the rich among you...' until He said: 'For the poor emigrants who were driven from their homes and their wealth, seeking bounty from Allah and pleasure...' Then He, Glorious, said: 'And those who settled in the city and faith before them love those who emigrate to them...' and this, as far as we know, is specifically for the Ansar. Then He said: 'And those who come after them say: Our Lord, forgive us and our brothers who preceded us in faith...'

This, and Allah knows best, is for those who come after them from the believers until the Day of Resurrection. And Bilal and his companions asked Umar ibn al-Khattab to divide what Allah had returned (fay') to them from Iraq and Syria, saying: 'Divide the lands among those who conquered them as the booty of armies is divided.' But Umar refused that and recited these verses to them, saying: 'Allah has made those who come after you partners in this fay'; if I were to divide it, nothing would remain for those after you.'

Abu Yusuf said: Some of my teachers narrated to me from Yazid ibn Habib: 'Umar wrote to Sa'd when he conquered Iraq: "To proceed: Your letter has reached me in which you mention that the people asked you to divide among them their spoils and what Allah has returned (fay'). So when this letter of mine reaches you, look at what the people have brought to you to the army of warhorses or wealth..."'
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage addresses the second option available to the imam upon conquering a territory by force: he may either divide the land and movable wealth among the warriors as booty, or he may leave the original inhabitants on the land and impose upon them a land tax (kharaj) and a poll tax (jizya). The commentary cites the practice of Caliph Umar (RA) when he conquered Iraq: he chose the latter option. The text then provides a lengthy excerpt from Imam Abu Yusuf's Kitab al-Kharaj, which records a debate between Umar and some companions, including Bilal (RA), who wanted the lands divided like ordinary booty. Umar refused, quoting several verses from Surah al-Hashr (59:7-10) which specify the recipients of fay' wealth: Allah, the Messenger, relatives, orphans, the needy, wayfarers, and then later generations of Muslims—the Muhajirun, the Ansar, and those who come after them. Umar argued that by dividing the land among the current conquerors, later Muslims would be deprived of any share in that wealth. Therefore, he kept the land as a permanent endowment (fay') whose revenue would benefit the entire Muslim community perpetually, including future generations. This decision became a foundational precedent in Hanafi fiqh regarding the treatment of conquered lands, establishing the imam's discretionary authority to choose between these two options based on public interest (maslahah).

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrar): The act of leaving the conquered land with its original inhabitants and imposing kharaj and jizya upon them.
الخراج (al-kharaj): A land tax imposed on the conquered land that remains in the hands of its original non-Muslim inhabitants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what option did Umar (RA) choose regarding the conquered lands of Iraq?
A) He divided them among the conquerors as booty.
B) He left them with the original inhabitants and imposed kharaj.
C) He gave them to the poor of the Muslims.
D) He sold them to the highest bidder.

Key Takeaway
The imam may either distribute conquered land as booty or leave it with its people and impose kharaj, as Umar did, based on Quranic verses that allocate fay' to all Muslims including later generations.

The Imam's Discretion in Dividing Conquered Land
Commentary on the Imam's options regarding land and prisoners in conquest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options the Imam has for conquered land (anwatan) and apply the Hanafi ruling based on the proofs from the Quran, the practice of Caliph Umar, and the principle of maslahah.

Core Idea
The Imam may either divide conquered land as spoils or leave it with inhabitants and impose jizya and kharaj.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the Hanafi position on how the Imam should handle land conquered by force. It presents two options—division among the army or leaving it with the original inhabitants—and supports both with the Quranic verses on fay' and the precedent of Umar ibn al-Khattab. The lesson will walk you through the ruling, its proofs, and the inter-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two options
The text states that the Imam has a choice: he may either divide the conquered land among the Muslim army as spoils, or he may leave the land with its original inhabitants and impose jizya (head tax) and kharaj (land tax) upon them.
These options apply to land conquered by force (maftuh anwatan).
2
Understand the Hanafi position
Both options are permissible (mubah). The Imam may choose based on maslahah (public interest). Al-Hidayah notes that division is preferable when the combatants are in need, and leaving it is preferable when they are not, so that it remains a resource for future Muslims.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Locate the dalil (proof)
The primary proof is from Surah al-Hashr (7-10), which describes that fay' (including conquered land) is for the benefit of all Muslims across generations, not just the present fighters. The phrase 'so that it does not become a monopoly among the wealthy from you' (kay la yakuna dulatan bayna al-aghniya' minkum) supports communal ownership.
The verses are qati' al-thubut (definitely transmitted) but zanni al-dalalah (open to interpretation).
4
Note the ikhtilaf (dispute)
The Shafi'i school holds that conquered land must be divided as spoils among the army, based on the general rule of booty division (Quran 8:41) and the Prophet's division of Khaybar. The Hanafi school responds that Umar's decision, based on the fay' verses and consultation, is authoritative, and Khaybar is distinguishable (movable property or unique case).
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in Hanafi law, conquered land becomes waqf for all Muslims, while in Shafi'i law it is private property of the conquerors.
5
Apply the ruling
When encountering a modern scenario of conquest, the Hanafi mufti would advise that the Imam may choose either option, with a preference towards preserving land as a public trust when the army does not urgently need it.
This discretion extends only to immovable property; movable spoils must be distributed.

أو أقر أهله عليه

قوله : أو أقرّ ؛ يعني الإمامُ بالخيار في المفتوح عنوة بين أن يقسمه على الجيش وبين أن يقر أهل ذلك المقام عليه، ويوظف عليهم جزية وخراجاً، هكذا فعله عمر رضي الله عنه حين فتح بلاد العراق، أخرجه ابن سعد في «الطبقات».

وفي كتاب «الخراج» للإمام أبي يوسف رضي الله عنه: «أما الفيء يا أمير المؤمنين فهو الخراج عندنا خراج الأرض ؛ لأنّ الله تبارك وتعالى يقول في كتابه: ﴿مَا أَفَاءَ اللَّهُ عَلَى رَسُولِهِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْقُرَى فَلِلَّهِ وَالرَّسُولِ وَلِذِي الْقُرْبَى وَالْيَتَامَى وَالْمَسَاكِينِ وَابْنِ السَّبِيلِ كَيْ لَا يَكُونَ دُولَةً بَيْنَ الْأَغْنِيَاءِ مِنْكُمْ﴾ [الحشر:7] إلى أن قال: ﴿لِلْفُقَرَاءِ الْمُهَاجِرِينَ الَّذِينَ أُخْرِجُوا مِنْ دِيَارِهِمْ وَأَمْوَالِهِمْ يَبْتَغُونَ فَضْلًا مِنَ اللَّهِ وَرِضْوَانًا﴾ [الحشر:8] ثم قال جل ذكره: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ تَبَوَّءُوا الدَّارَ وَالْإِيمَانَ مِنْ قَبْلِهِمْ يُحِبُّونَ مَنْ هَاجَرَ إِلَيْهِمْ﴾ [الحشر:9]، وهذا فيما بلغنا في الأنصار خاصة، ثم قال تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ جَاءُوا مِنْ بَعْدِهِمْ يَقُولُونَ رَبَّنَا اغْفِرْ لَنَا وَلِإِخْوَانِنَا الَّذِينَ سَبَقُونَا بِالْإِيمَانِ﴾ [الحشر:10] فهذا والله أعلم لمن جاءَ بعدهم من المؤمنين إلى يوم القيامة، وقد سأل بلال وأصحابه عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه قسمة ما أفاء الله عليهم من العراق والشام، وقالوا: قسموا الأرضين بين الذين افتتحوها كما تقسّم غنيمة العساكر، فأبي عمر رضي الله عنه ذلك وتلى عليهم هذه الآيات، وقال: قد أشرك الله لكم الذين يأتون من بعدكم في هذا الفيء، فلو قسمته لم يبق لمن بعدكم شيء.

قال أبو يوسف: حدثني بعض أشياخي عن يزيد بن حبيب: «إنَّ عمر رضي الله عنه كتب إلى سعد حين افتتح العراق، أما بعد؛ فقد بلغني كتابك تذكر فيه أن الناس سألوك أن تقسّم بينهم مغانمهم وما أفاء الله، فإذا أتاك كتابي هذا فانظر ما أجلب الناسُ به عليك إلى العسكر من كراع أو مال، فأقسمه بين من حضر من المسلمين، وأترك الأرضين والأنهار بعمالنا، ليكون ذلك من عطيات المسلمين، فإنك إن قسمته بين من حضر لم يكن لمن بعدهم شيء.

وحدثني الليث بن سعد عن حبيب بن ثابت: إن أصحاب محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم وجماعة من المسلمين أرادوا أن يقسم عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه الشام كما قسم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم خيبر، وإنه كان أشد الناس عليه في ذلك الزبير بن العوام وبلال رضي الله عنهما، فقال عمر رضي الله عنه: إذا أترك من بعدكم من المسلمين بلا شيء لهم، ثم قال: اللهم اكفني بلالاً وأصحابه، قال: ورأى المسلمون أن الطاعون الذي أصابهم بعمواس كان من دعوة عمر قال: وتركهم لله ذمة يؤدون الخراج إلى المسلمين». انتهى كلامه

وفي «الهداية»: قيل: الأول: - أي القسمة بين الجيش - أولى عند حاجة الغانمين، والثاني: عند عدم الحاجة؛ ليكون عدة في الزمان الثاني، وهذا في العقار، أما في المنقول المجرد لا يجوز المنّ بالرد عليهم؛ لأنه لم يرد به الشرع فيه.

قوله: بجزية وخراج؛ الجزية - بالكسر -: ما يُوظفه الإمام على ذوات الكفار مشاهرة أو مسانهة والخراج - بالفتح -: ما يُوظفه على أراضيهم.

قوله: على أحد الأمرين؛ فيه إشارة إما إلى ما وقع من الاختلاف فيما بين أن المعطوف الثاني، هل هو معطوف على المعطوف الأول أو على المعطوف عليه، وإما إشارة إلى أن قوله: «قسم» أو «أقر» في قوة فعل أحد الأمرين؛ لكون عطف أقر بـ«أو»، فقوله: «قتل...الخ عطف على الحاصل.

قوله: أو استرقهم؛ من الاسترقاق، يعني الإمام مخير في الكفار الذين أسرهم جيش الإسلام بين ثلاثة أمور يختار منها ما شاء حسبما رآه مصلحة:
"Or leave its people upon it." His statement: "Or leave" means the Imam has a choice regarding what is conquered by force between dividing it among the army and leaving the people of that place upon it, imposing upon them jizya and kharaj. Thus did 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, when he conquered the lands of Iraq, as recorded by Ibn Sa'd in al-Tabaqat. In the Kitab al-Kharaj of Imam Abu Yusuf, may Allah be pleased with him: "As for the fay', O Commander of the Faithful, it is the kharaj according to us, the kharaj of the land, because Allah, Blessed and Exalted, says in His Book: 'What Allah has returned to His Messenger from the people of the towns belongs to Allah and to the Messenger and to the near of kin and to orphans and the needy and the wayfarer, so that it does not become a monopoly among the wealthy among you' [al-Hashr:7] until He said: 'For the poor emigrants who were expelled from their homes and their properties, seeking bounty from Allah and [His] approval' [al-Hashr:8]. Then He, Majestic in His mention, said: 'And those who were settled in the Home [al-Madinah] and [adopted] faith before them, love those who emigrate to them' [al-Hashr:9], and this according to what has reached us is specifically for the Ansar. Then He, Exalted, said: 'And those who came after them say: Our Lord, forgive us and our brothers who preceded us in faith' [al-Hashr:10]. This, and Allah knows best, is for those who come after them from the believers until the Day of Resurrection. And Bilal and his companions asked 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, to divide what Allah had returned to them from Iraq and Syria, and they said: Divide the lands among those who conquered them just as the spoils of the armies are divided. But 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, refused that and recited these verses to them, and said: Allah has made you share with those who come after you in this fay', so if I were to divide it, nothing would remain for those after you. Abu Yusuf said: Some of my teachers narrated to me from Yazid ibn Habib: ''Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, wrote to Sa'd when he conquered Iraq: 'To proceed; your letter has reached me in which you mention that the people asked you to divide among them their spoils and what Allah has returned. So when this letter of mine reaches you, look at what the people have brought to you in the army of horses or property, and divide it among those present of the Muslims, and leave the lands and rivers with our workers so that it may be part of the stipends of the Muslims. For if you divide it among those present, nothing will remain for those after them.' And al-Layth ibn Sa'd narrated to me from Habib ibn Thabit: Indeed the Companions of Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, and a group of Muslims wanted 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, to divide Syria just as the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, divided Khaybar. And the most severe people against him in that were al-Zubayr ibn al-'Awwam and Bilal, may Allah be pleased with them. 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'Then I would leave the Muslims after you with nothing for them.' Then he said: 'O Allah, suffice me against Bilal and his companions.' He said: And the Muslims saw that the plague that afflicted them at 'Amwas was from the supplication of 'Umar. He said: 'And he left them as a dhimma for Allah, paying kharaj to the Muslims.'" End of his speech. And in al-Hidayah: It is said: The first—i.e., division among the army—is preferable when the combatants are in need, and the second when there is no need, so that it may be a reserve for the second era. This applies to immovable property. As for movable property, it is not permissible to show favor by returning it to them because the Shari'ah has not permitted it in this case. His statement: "with jizya and kharaj." Jizya—with a kasra—is what the Imam imposes on the persons of the disbelievers annually or monthly, and kharaj—with a fatha—is what he imposes on their lands. His statement: "regarding one of the two matters." In it is an indication either of the difference that occurred among grammarians regarding whether the second conjoined element is conjoined to the first conjoined element or to the thing conjoined upon, or an indication that his statement: "divide" or "leave" is in the strength of performing one of the two matters, since the conjunction of "leave" is with "or", so his statement: "kill, etc." is conjoined to the accomplished [matter]. His statement: "or enslave them" from istirqaq, meaning the Imam has a choice regarding the disbelievers whom the army of Islam has captured between three matters, choosing from them whatever he wishes according to what he sees as beneficial:
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary (sharh) on the text of Sharh al-Wiqayah, expanding on the rulings related to the distribution of spoils (ghanimah) and conquered lands. The passage begins by explaining the phrase 'or leave its people upon it,' which refers to the Imam's option when a territory is conquered by force (anwatan). The Imam may either divide the land among the Muslim army as a spoil, or leave the original inhabitants in place and impose two financial obligations: jizya (a head tax on non-Muslims) and kharaj (a land tax). This was the practice of Caliph Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) after the conquest of Iraq, as recorded by Ibn Sa'd. The text then quotes extensively from Imam Abu Yusuf's Kitab al-Kharaj, where he discusses the nature of fay' (booty that comes without direct military action) and argues that it is essentially kharaj from land. He cites verses from Surah al-Hashr (verses 7-10) to show that fay' is not to be distributed only among the wealthy or the present generation, but belongs to all Muslims across time: the poor emigrants, the Ansar, and those who come after them. Abu Yusuf narrates that Bilal and some Companions requested Umar to divide the conquered lands of Iraq and Syria as spoils, but Umar refused, reciting these verses and stating that he would not deprive future generations of Muslims. Umar wrote to Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas instructing him to distribute movable spoils among the army but to keep the lands and rivers under state control for the benefit of all Muslims. Another narration describes the dispute with al-Zubayr and Bilal, and Umar's famous supplication that the plague at 'Amwas was a result of his prayer. The commentary then cites al-Hidayah, which discusses the preference between the two options: division of land is preferable when the combatants are in need, while leaving the land in place is preferable when there is no need, so that it serves as a resource for the future. This applies only to immovable property (aqar); for movable property, returning it to the original owners as a favor is not permitted because there is no textual basis. The passage then defines jizya and kharaj: jizya is a tax on the persons of non-Muslims, paid monthly or yearly; kharaj is a tax on their lands. Finally, it explains the grammatical structure of the original text, noting that the options regarding prisoners (kill, enslave, or free as dhimmis) are coordinated with the earlier options regarding land.

Key Terms
المفتوح عنوة (al-maftūḥ 'anwatan): Territory captured by force through military conquest.
الجزية (al-jizyah): A tax imposed on the persons (dhimmis) of non-Muslims in exchange for protection and exemption from military service, paid annually or monthly.
الخراج (al-kharāj): A land tax imposed on agricultural land owned by non-Muslims (or land left in their hands) in conquered territories.
الفيء (al-fay'): Wealth or property acquired from non-Muslims without direct military action (or in this context, including conquered land as per Umar's policy).
الاسترقاق (al-istirqāq): Enslavement of prisoners of war.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Imam must always divide the land among the army.
B) The Imam must always leave the land with the inhabitants and impose kharaj.
C) The Imam has a choice (mubah) between the two options based on maslahah.
D) The land must be divided equally between the army and the inhabitants.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school gives the Imam full discretion to either divide conquered land as spoils or leave it with its inhabitants and impose jizya and kharaj, based on the Quran and the precedent of Umar.

The Prohibition of Mann and Fida: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ransoming Captives
Explains the prohibition of mann and fida with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mann and fida, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding fida, and apply the mufta bihi position when evaluating a scenario involving captive exchange.

Core Idea
Mann is absolutely prohibited; fida is generally prohibited but permitted when Muslims have a genuine need.

The imam has several options when dealing with captive infidels: killing, enslaving, or leaving them as dhimmis. But what about releasing them for ransom? The matn of al-Wiqayah states that mann (freeing without compensation) and fida (ransom) are not allowed. However, an important intra-Hanafi dispute arises: Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani permits fida when Muslims are in need, citing the precedent of the captives of Badr. This lesson unpacks that dispute and clarifies the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three options for the imam
The passage lists three established options: killing, enslaving, or leaving them as dhimmis. Understand these as the baseline before considering mann or fida.
These are the primary choices; mann and fida are exceptions.
2
Define mann and fida
Learn the technical definitions: mann is release without anything; fida is release in exchange for money or a Muslim captive.
These terms are specific to captives.
3
State the matn ruling
The matn prohibits both mann and fida absolutely. The commentator explains 'لا يجوز المن ولا فداهم'.
This is the default position in the madhhab.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad permits fida if there is a need, citing the Badr incident where Abu Bakr advised ransom but the Quranic verse rebuked it. Understand the difference of opinion with the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) who hold absolute prohibition.
The dispute is about the applicability of the Badr exception.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that mann is forbidden, fida is generally forbidden but allowed when needed, following Imam Muhammad's view as it aligns with maslahah.
The commentator notes that Muhammad's opinion is taken when there is benefit.

أحدها: أن يقتلهم فيؤمن من شرهم، ويكون عبرة لغيرهم، وقد ثبت ذلك عن النبي يوم فتح مكة، ويوم بدر، ويوم بني قريظة، فقد أخرج الشيخان : «إنّ النبي أمر بقتل ابن خطل، وكان قد تعلّق بأستار الكعبة). وأخرج أصحابُ السُّننِ والبيهقي وغيرهم: «أمره بقتل بني قريظة – وهم قبيلة من يهود المدينة - وسبي نسائهم وذراريهم». وأخرج أبو داود في «المراسيل»: «إنّه صلى الله عليه وسلم أمر بقتل مطعم بن عدي، والنضر بن الحارث، وعقبة بن أبي معيط حين أسروا يوم بدر، وفي رواية: «طعمة بن عدي»، موضع مطعم، وهو الصحيح، فإنّ مطعماً قد كان مات بمكة قبل بدر.
وثانيها : أن يجعلهم عبيداً أرقاء، فإن أسلموا بعد ذلك لم يسقط عنهم الرق؛ لأن الرق جزاء الكفر الأصلي، فلا يسقط ما لم يعتق ، بخلاف ما إذا أسلموا قبل الاستيلاء، حيث لا يجوز استرقاقهم ولا قتلهم. كذا في «العناية».
وثالثها: أن يتركهم أحراراً يؤدون الجزية ويصيرون أهل ذمة ، كما فعل عمر حين افتتح بلاد العراق على ما مر وهذا الثالث، وفي الثاني غير مشركي العرب والمرتدين، فإنّه لا يجوز ضرب الجزية عليهم ولا الاسترقاق على ما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى.
(ونُفي منهم وفداؤهم).
المن : أن يترك الأسير الكافر من غير أن يؤخذ منه شيئاً.
والفداء : أن يترك ويأخذ منه مالاً ، أو أسيرا مسلما منهم في مقابلته.
قوله : أي ليكونوا ؛ وقيل : معنى قوله : ذمّة لنا ؛ حقاً واجباً لنا عليهم من الجزية والخراج ؛ فإنّ الذمة الحق والعهد والأمان ؛ ولذا يُسمَّى الكافر ذميّاً.
قوله : ونفى ؛ بصيغة المجهول ؛ أي لا يجوز المن على أسارى الكفار بأن يتركهم مجانا من غير قتل ولا استرقاق ولا ضرب جزية، ولا يجوز فداهم. وذكر محمد له في «السير الكبير»: إنه لا بأس به إذا كان بالمسلمين حاجة استدلالاً بفداء أسارى بدر، فإنّه قد أسر يوم بدر سبعون رجلاً من الكفّار، فاستشار رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أصحابه الله في شأنهم، فأشار عمر بقتلهم، وأشار أبو بكر له إلى أخذ الفداء منهم وتركهم، فمالَ رسولُ الله له إلى رأي أبي بكر ، وتركهم بعد أخذ المال منهم، فنَزَلَ الوحي بتصويب رأي عمر وقال الله له معاتباً : مَا كَانَ لِنَي أَن يَكُونَ لَهُ أَسْرَىٰ حَتَّى يُشْخِنَ فِي الْأَرْضِ تُرِيدُونَ عَرَضَ الدُّنْيَا وَاللهُ يُرِيدُ الآخِرَةُ ) ، الآيات في سورة الأنفال، أخرجه مسلم وأبو داود وغيرهما مطوّلاً ومختصراً.
قوله : أن يترك ؛ بصيغة المجهول، فما بعده نائب فاعله، أو بصيغة المعروف، وفاعله الضمير الراجع إلى الإمام، وما بعده مفعوله، وهذا هو الأظهر.
One of them: that he kills them, so their evil is warded off, and it becomes a lesson for others. This is proven from the Prophet on the day of the conquest of Mecca, on the day of Badr, and on the day of Banu Qurayzah. For the Two Shaykhs narrated: 'The Prophet ordered the killing of Ibn Khatal, who was clinging to the curtains of the Ka'bah.' And the authors of the Sunan and al-Bayhaqi and others narrated: 'He ordered the killing of Banu Qurayzah—a tribe of the Jews of Medina—and the captivity of their women and children.' And Abu Dawud narrated in al-Marasil: 'He ordered the killing of Mut'im ibn 'Adi, al-Nadr ibn al-Harith, and 'Uqbah ibn Abi Mu'ayt when they were captured on the day of Badr.' In another narration: 'T'umah ibn 'Adi' in place of Mut'im, and that is correct, for Mut'im had died in Mecca before Badr.
And the second: that he makes them slaves; if they accept Islam after that, slavery is not lifted from them because slavery is the penalty for original disbelief, so it does not fall until they are emancipated, unlike if they become Muslims before being overpowered, for then it is not permissible to enslave or kill them. Thus in al-'Inayah.
And the third: that he leaves them free, paying jizyah and becoming people of dhimma, as 'Umar did when he conquered the lands of Iraq as previously mentioned. And this is the third option; and the second does not include the polytheists of the Arabs and the apostates, for it is not permissible to impose jizyah on them or enslave them, as will come, if Allah wills.
(And they are not granted mann nor fida).
Mann: that the captive infidel is released without taking anything from him.
Fida: that he is released and money is taken from him, or a Muslim captive from them in exchange.
His saying: 'that they be'—or it is said: the meaning of his saying: 'dhimma for us' is a right obligatory for us upon them of jizyah and kharaj; for dhimma means right, covenant, and security; thus the infidel is called a dhimmi.
His saying: 'And they are not granted mann' in the passive; meaning it is not permissible to grant mann to infidel captives by releasing them for free without killing, enslaving, or imposing jizyah, nor is their fida permissible. And Muhammad mentioned in al-Siyar al-Kabir: 'There is no harm in it if the Muslims have a need, using as evidence the ransom of the captives of Badr.' For on the day of Badr, seventy infidels were taken captive, and the Messenger of Allah consulted his Companions about them. 'Umar advised killing them, and Abu Bakr advised taking ransom from them and releasing them. So the Messenger inclined to Abu Bakr's opinion and released them after taking money from them. Then revelation came confirming 'Umar's opinion, and Allah said to him rebukingly: 'It is not for a prophet to have captives until he has thoroughly subdued the land. You desire the goods of the world, but Allah desires the Hereafter.' The verses in Surah al-Anfal. Narrated by Muslim, Abu Dawud, and others in lengthy and abridged forms.
His saying: 'that he releases'—in the passive, so what follows is its deputy subject, or in the active, and its agent is the pronoun referring to the imam, and what follows is its object. And this is the more apparent.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary on the matn of al-Wiqayah regarding the options available to the imam when dealing with captive infidels. It is an expansion of the ruling on mann and fida. The passage first outlines three established options: killing, enslaving, or leaving them as dhimmis with jizyah. These are proven from the Prophet's actions at the conquest of Mecca (killing Ibn Khatal), at Badr (killing specific captives), and at Banu Qurayzah (killing and enslaving). The second option of enslavement is permanent even if they later accept Islam, because slavery is a penalty for original disbelief, unlike if they accept Islam before capture. The third option of making them dhimmis is analogous to 'Umar's practice in Iraq. The matn then says 'And they are not granted mann nor fida.' The commentator defines mann as releasing without compensation, and fida as releasing in exchange for money or a Muslim captive. He clarifies that the matn prohibits both mann and fida absolutely. However, he reports an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in al-Siyar al-Kabir permits fida if Muslims are in need, citing the incident of the captives of Badr. At Badr, the Prophet consulted the Companions; 'Umar advised execution, Abu Bakr advised ransom. The Prophet initially followed Abu Bakr and took ransom, but then the Quranic verse (al-Anfal 67) rebuked that, affirming 'Umar's view. From this, the majority Hanafi view (mufta bihi) is that mann is never allowed, and fida is also not allowed in ordinary circumstances, but when there is a clear benefit to Muslims (like need), fida may be permissible as an exception, following Muhammad's opinion. The commentator also notes that the phrase 'that he releases' is better understood in the active voice with the imam as subject.

Key Terms
المن (al-mann): Releasing an infidel captive without taking any compensation (money or exchange).
الفداء (al-fida'): Releasing a captive in exchange for money or a Muslim captive held by the enemy.
أسرى (asra): Captives taken from the enemy during warfare.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn text 'ونُفي منهم وفداؤهم', what is the ruling on mann (freeing captives without ransom)?
A) It is allowed
B) It is prohibited
C) It is only allowed if the captive converts to Islam
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
Mann is always prohibited; fida is generally prohibited but may be allowed when Muslims have a genuine need, based on Imam Muhammad's opinion.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules

The Hanafi Ruling on Gratuitous Release and Ransom of Prisoners of War
Explains the Hanafi ruling on mann and fida' with proofs and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on al-mann and al-fida', identify the intra-Hanafi variation, and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof.

Core Idea
Gratuitous release and ransom of enemy captives are generally prohibited in the Hanafi school, based on Quranic abrogation and the principle of repelling harm.

The treatment of prisoners of war was a matter of early community disagreement. This passage from the Sharh al-Wiqayah tackles the core question: may the imam gratuitously release or ransom captives? The Hanafi ruling, its proof, and the counter-argument from the Shafi'i school are presented, along with an important intra-Hanafi opinion from Imam Muhammad. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school prioritizes definitive textual evidence over prophetic practice when abrogation is established.

Guided Path
1
Define the terms and options
Clarify what al-mann (gratuitous release) and al-fida' (ransom) mean, and note the third option of making captives dhimmis. These definitions set the stage for the legal assessment.
The third option (making them dhimmis) is generally accepted by all schools.
2
State the general Hanafi position
From the Zahir al-Riwayah, both al-mann and al-fida' are prohibited (haram). This is the relied-upon position in the madhhab.
The text uses 'la yajuz' (not permissible) for both.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi variation
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in al-Siyar al-Kabir permits both if the Muslims are in need, citing the Badr incident. This shows flexibility within the school.
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf maintain the prohibition.
4
Follow the Shafi'i proof
Imam al-Shafi'i allows mann and fida' if the imam sees a maslahah, using prophetic examples: the captives of Hunayn, Abu al-'As, and the ransom at Badr.
These examples are well-attested in hadith.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that these examples are abrogated by later revelation (Quran 9:5) and that fida' aids disbelief. The principle of repelling harm takes precedence over potential benefits.
The objection about enslavement and jizyah is answered by consensus and hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجهاد / باب المغنم وقسمته
ونُفي منهم وفداؤهم
أي ليكونوا أهل ذمة لنا.
(ونُفي منهم وفداؤهم).
المن : أن يترك الأسير الكافر من غير أن يؤخذ منه شيئاً.
والفداء : أن يترك ويأخذ منه مالاً ، أو أسيرا مسلما منهم في مقابلته.
وثالثها: أن يتركهم أحراراً يؤدون الجزية ويصيرون أهل ذمة ، كما فعل عمر حين افتتح بلاد العراق على ما مر وهذا الثالث، وفي الثاني غير مشركي العرب والمرتدين، فإنّه لا يجوز ضرب الجزية عليهم ولا الاسترقاق على ما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى.
[1] قوله : أي ليكونوا ؛ وقيل : معنى قوله : ذمّة لنا ؛ حقاً واجباً لنا عليهم من الجزية والخراج ؛ فإنّ الذمة الحق والعهد والأمان ؛ ولذا يُسمَّى الكافر ذميّاً. [2] قوله : ونفى ؛ بصيغة المجهول ؛ أي لا يجوز المن على أسارى الكفار بأن يتركهم مجانا من غير قتل ولا استرقاق ولا ضرب جزية، ولا يجوز فداهم. وذكر محمد له في «السير الكبير»: إنه لا بأس به إذا كان بالمسلمين حاجة استدلالاً بفداء أسارى بدر، فإنّه قد أسر يوم بدر سبعون رجلاً من الكفّار، فاستشار رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أصحابه في شأنهم، فأشار عمر بقتلهم، وأشار أبو بكر إلى أخذ الفداء منهم وتركهم، فمالَ رسولُ الله إلى رأي أبي بكر ، وتركهم بعد أخذ المال منهم ، فنَزَلَ الوحي بتصويب رأي عمر وقال الله معاتباً : مَا كَانَ لِنَبِيٍّ أَن يَكُونَ لَهُ أَسْرَىٰ حَتَّىٰ يُثْخِنَ فِي الْأَرْضِ تُرِيدُونَ عَرَضَ الدُّنْيَا وَاللهُ يُرِيدُ الآخِرَةَ ، الآيات في سورة الأنفال، أخرجه مسلم وأبو داود وغيرهما مطوّلاً ومختصراً.
[3] قوله : أن يترك ؛ بصيغة المجهول، فما بعده نائب فاعله، أو بصيغة المعروف، وفاعله الضمير الراجع إلى الإمام، وما بعده مفعوله، وهذا هو الأظهر.
ففي المَنْ خلافُ الشَّافِعِي
[1] قوله : خلاف الشافعي له ; فإنّه يجوز عنده إن رآه الإمام مصلحة ; لثبوتِ ذلك عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم غير مرة ، فقـد مـن على سبي حنين سنة فتح مكة كما أخرجه البخاري، ومن على صهره أبي العاص بن الربيع زوج زينب بنت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حين أسر ببدر كافراً، كما أخرجه أبو داود وابن سعد والحاكم وغيرهم. وتمن مَنَّ عليه يوم بدر على ما ذكره ابن هشام في «سيرته» نقلاً عن ابن إسحاق : عمرو بن عبد الله الجمحي، والمطلب بن حنطب. وأجاب من منع المنّ بأنه منسوخ بآية سورة براءة : ﴿ فَاقْتُلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ حَيْثُ وَجَدتُمُوهُمْ وَخُذُوهُمْ وَاحْصُرُوهُمْ وَاقْعُدُوا لَهُمْ كُلَّ مَرْصَدٍ ﴾ . فإن قلت : فينبغي عدم جواز الاسترقاق وتركهم ذمة لنا أيضاً ; لأنّ الآية ليس فيها إلا ذكر القتل.
قلت : إنما تركنا العمل بظاهر الآية في هذا الباب بالإجماع وبالأخبار المشهورة في جواز الاسترقاق وضرب الجزية.
[2] قوله : وأما الفداء... الخ ; استدل من جوز الفداء مطلقاً بقصة أسارى بدر على ما مر وبما أخرجه مسلم وأبو داود أنّ النبي فدى رجلين من المسلمين برجل من المشركين، وفي الباب حديث آخر أخرجه مسلم. ومن منعه استدلّ بأنّ فيه معونة الكفر; لأنه يعود حرباً علينا، ودفع شرّ حربه أولى من استنفاذ الأسير المسلم ، ومن أخذ المال كذا قالوا.
وأنت تعلم أن المصير إلى ما ثبت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في هذه المسائل المن والفداء بالمال والنفس أحق ما لم يثبت نسخه.
Book of Jihad / Chapter of Booty and its Division
And they are not to be shown grace nor ransomed
That is, to become ahl al-dhimmah for us.
(And not shown grace nor ransomed)
Al-Mann: to leave the infidel captive without taking anything from him.
Al-Fida': to leave him and take money from him, or a Muslim captive from them in exchange.
And a third: to leave them free such that they pay jizyah and become ahl al-dhimmah, as 'Umar did when he conquered the lands of Iraq as previously mentioned. This is the third option. And regarding the second [option, i.e., taking jizyah], it does not apply to polytheist Arabs and apostates, for it is not permissible to impose jizyah on them nor to enslave them, as will come, God willing.
[1] He said: 'That is, to become' and it was said: the meaning of his saying: 'dhimmah for us' is a right obligatory for us upon them of jizyah and kharaj; for al-dhimmah means right, covenant, and security; hence the infidel is called dhimmi.
[2] He said: 'And not shown grace' in the passive voice; i.e., it is not permissible to show grace to infidel captives by leaving them free without killing, enslaving, or imposing jizyah, nor is it permissible to ransom them. And Muhammad mentioned in al-Siyar al-Kabir: there is no harm in it if the Muslims are in need, using as evidence the ransom of the captives of Badr. For on the day of Badr, seventy men of the infidels were captured, and the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, consulted his companions about their affair. 'Umar advised killing them, and Abu Bakr advised taking ransom and releasing them. The Messenger of Allah inclined to Abu Bakr's opinion and released them after taking money from them. Then revelation came affirming 'Umar's opinion, and Allah said, rebuking him: 'It is not for a prophet to have captives until he has made slaughter in the land. You desire the goods of the world, while Allah desires the Hereafter' – verses from Surah al-Anfal, reported by Muslim, Abu Dawud, and others both in full and summary.
[3] He said: 'that he releases' in the passive voice, so what follows is the agent; or in the active voice, its subject is the pronoun referring to the imam, and what follows is its object. This is more apparent.
Regarding al-mann, there is disagreement with al-Shafi'i.
[1] He said: 'Disagreement with al-Shafi'i in this; for he permits it if the imam sees it as a maslahah, because it has been established from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, more than once. He showed grace to the captives of Hunayn in the year of the conquest of Mecca, as reported by al-Bukhari, and showed grace to his son-in-law Abu al-'As ibn al-Rabi', the husband of Zaynab, the daughter of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he was captured as an infidel at Badr, as reported by Abu Dawud, Ibn Sa'd, al-Hakim, and others. And among those upon whom he showed grace on the day of Badr, as mentioned by Ibn Hisham in his Sirah from Ibn Ishaq: 'Amr ibn 'Abdullah al-Jumahi and al-Muttalib ibn Hantab.' And those who prohibit al-mann replied that it is abrogated by the verse of Surah Bara'ah: 'Then kill the polytheists wherever you find them and take them and besiege them and lie in wait for them at every place of ambush.' If you say: then it should not be permissible to enslave them or leave them as dhimmah for us, because the verse only mentions killing. I say: we only abandon the apparent meaning of the verse in this chapter due to consensus and well-known reports about the permissibility of enslavement and imposition of jizyah.
[2] He said: 'As for al-fida'...' Those who permit fida' absolutely used as evidence the story of the captives of Badr as mentioned, and what Muslim and Abu Dawud reported that the Prophet ransomed two men from the Muslims for one man from the polytheists. There is another hadith on this topic reported by Muslim. Those who prohibit it used as evidence that it involves aiding disbelief, because he returns to fight us, and repelling the harm of his war is more important than rescuing the Muslim captive or taking money. And you know that following what has been established from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, in these matters of al-mann and al-fida' with wealth and life is more appropriate as long as its abrogation has not been established.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the treatment of enemy prisoners of war, specifically the permissibility of gratuitous release (al-mann) and ransom (al-fida'). The author begins by defining these terms: al-mann is releasing a captive without taking anything, while al-fida' is releasing him in exchange for money or a Muslim captive. A third option is to release them as dhimmis paying jizyah. The commentary then states the general Hanafi ruling: both al-mann and al-fida' are not permissible (la yajuz). However, Imam Muhammad in al-Siyar al-Kabir permits them if the Muslims are in need, citing the incident of the prisoners of Badr. The text then reproduces the famous story of the consultation at Badr, where Abu Bakr advised ransom, Umar advised execution, and the Prophet initially followed Abu Bakr, but then revelation came rebuking them and approving Umar's view. This establishes the abrogation of ransom and gratuitous release. The author then addresses the Shafi'i position: Shafi'i allows mann if the imam deems it a maslahah, citing examples from the Prophet's life such as the captives of Hunayn and Abu al-'As. The Hanafi response is that those instances are abrogated by the verse from Surah Bara'ah (9:5) ordering the killing of polytheists. The author anticipates an objection: if the verse commands killing, then why is enslavement and jizyah allowed? The answer is that those are established by consensus and well-known hadith. Similarly, for fida', the Shafi'i proof from the Badr story and a hadith about ransoming two Muslims for one polytheist is rejected by the Hanafis on the grounds that it aids disbelief, and repelling the harm of war takes precedence over the benefit of ransoming. The passage concludes with a note that following the established sunnah in these matters is most appropriate unless abrogation is proven.

Key Terms
المنّ (al-mann): Releasing a captive without taking anything in return
الفداء (al-fida'): Releasing a captive in exchange for money or a Muslim captive
أهل ذمة (ahl al-dhimmah): Non-Muslim subjects of an Islamic state who pay jizyah and enjoy protection
أسارى (usara): Prisoners of war

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the general ruling on gratuitous release (al-mann) of enemy prisoners?
A) Permissible if the imam sees a maslahah
B) Not permissible
C) Permissible only in exchange for Muslim prisoners
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits gratuitous release and ransom of enemy captives as a general rule, based on the Quranic rebuke of the Badr ransom and the principle of not aiding disbelief, though Imam Muhammad allowed it under need.

Temporal Condition and Need: Ransoming Captives in Hanafi Jihad Law
Super-commentary on the ikhtilaf regarding ransoming captives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ransoming captives with money after the war, identify the condition of need that permits it, and distinguish the Hanafi position from that of Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
After war ends, ransom with money is haram unless there is need; ransom with Muslim captives is permissible according to the preferred Hanafi view.

The issue of ransoming captives after battle has been a point of inter-madhhab disagreement, particularly between the Hanafis and Shafi'is. In this passage, the commentator refines earlier statements by clarifying that while ransom with money is generally prohibited after the war ends, it becomes permissible in cases of need, and ransom with Muslim captives is accepted in the relied-upon view. Let us unpack the evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its temporal condition
Determine the ruling for ransom before and after the war ends. The verse from Surah Muhammad provides the temporal boundary: 'until the war lays down its burdens.'
2
State the Hanafi position and its condition
After the war, ransom with money is haram by consensus of the three Hanafi imams, except when there is a need (hajah). This exception is based on later fatwa authorities.
Ransom with Muslim captives is permissible according to the more apparent narrations.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note the differences among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding ransom with Muslim captives and the timing (before/after division).
4
Analyze the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that ransom with money is permissible absolutely, citing the apparent meaning of the verse and prophetic practice.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response and tarjih
The Hanafi response argues that the verse is conditioned by 'until the war lays down its burdens,' which limits the permissibility to before the war ends. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) incorporates the exception of need.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقبل أن تضع الحرب أوزارها يجوز بالمال لا بالأسير المسلم، وبعده لا يجوز بالمال بإجماع علمائنا ، وبالنفس لا يجوز عند أبي حنيفة
ثم اعلم أن كلام الشارح لاله هاهنا ، وكذا كلام مؤلّف «الدرر شرح الغرر» حاكم بأن قبل الفراغ من الحرب جاز الفداء بالمال لا بالأسير المسلم، وبعده لا يجوز بالمال عند علمائنا الثلاثة ولا بالنفس عند الإمام، وفي رواية عن أبي يوسف وعند محمد ، وفي رواية عن أبي يوسف الله يجوز ، وعند الشافعي له يجوز مطلقا. وذكر ابن كمال ومؤلف «النهر» إنّ الفرق بين قوله الفراغ من الحرب وبين ما بعده لا يفهم من كلامهم. وقال في «جامع الرموز»: نفي فداهم إلى إطلاقهم ببدل، وهو إما مال، وذا لا يجوز في المشهور، ولا بأس به عند الحاجة على ما في «السير الكبير»، وقال محمد ه : لا بأس به إذا كان بحيث لا يرجى منه النسلُ كالشيخ الفاني، كما في «الاختيار»، وإمّا أسير مسلم، وذا لا يجوز عنده ويجوز عندهما ، والأوّل الصحيح كما في «الزاد»، لكن في «المحيط»: إنّه يجوز في ظاهر الرواية ، وفي «الاختيار»: قال الكرخي : إنّه لا يجوز عند أبي يوسف له إلا قبل القسمة ، ويجوز عند محمد له مطلقاً. وذكر الزيلعي في «شرح الكنز » ) : إن جواز الفداء بالأسير المسلم أظهر الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة له ، وذكر في «الفتح») : إنّه قولهما وقولُ الأئمة الثلاثة، وإنّه ثبت عن رسول الله الله في «صحیح مسلم»، قال في رد المحتار (۳) : وعلى هـذا فقول المتون : حرام فداؤهم مقيد بالفداء بالمال عند عدم الحاجة، أما الفداء بالمال عند الحاجة أو بأسرى المسلمين فهو جائز. ١ ] قوله : فقبل أن تضع الحرب ؛ اقتباس من قوله علة : فَإِمَّا مَنَا بَعْدُ وَإِمَّا فِدَاءً حَتَّى تَضَعَ الحَرْبُ أَوْزَارَهَا ) : أي آلاتها وأثقالها التي لا يقوم الحرب إلا بها، كالسلاح والخيل، وهو إشارة إلى انقضاء الحرب والفراغ منه.
(٤)
Before the war lays down its burdens, ransom is permissible with money but not with a Muslim captive; after it, ransom with money is not permissible by the consensus of our scholars, and with a [Muslim] person it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa. Then know that the expression of the commentator here, and likewise the expression of the author of al-Durar Sharh al-Ghurar, rules that before the cessation of war, ransom with money is permissible but not with a Muslim captive; after it, ransom with money is not permissible according to our three imams, nor with a person according to the Imam. In one narration from Abu Yusuf and according to Muhammad, and in another narration from Abu Yusuf, it is permissible; and according to al-Shafi'i, it is permissible absolutely. Ibn Kamal and the author of al-Nahr mentioned that the difference between before the cessation of war and after it is not understood from their words. And it is said in Jami' al-Rumuz: The prohibition of ransoming them is absolute unless by way of exchange, which is either money—this is not permissible in the well-known view, but there is no harm in it when needed, as in al-Siyar al-Kabir; and Muhammad said: There is no harm in it if there is no hope of progeny from him, like a decrepit old man, as in al-Ikhtiyar—or a Muslim captive, which is not permissible according to him [Abu Hanifa] and permissible according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. The first is the correct view as in al-Zad, but in al-Muhit: It is permissible in the apparent transmission. And in al-Ikhtiyar, al-Karkhi said: It is not permissible according to Abu Yusuf except before division, and it is permissible according to Muhammad absolutely. And al-Zayla'i in Sharh al-Kanz mentioned that the permissibility of ransom with a Muslim captive is the more apparent of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa; and it is mentioned in al-Fath that it is the view of the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] and the view of the three imams, and that it is established from the Messenger of Allah in Sahih Muslim. He said in Radd al-Muhtar: Upon this, the statement of the texts that their ransom is prohibited is restricted to ransom with money when there is no need; as for ransom with money when needed or with Muslim captives, it is permissible. [Footnote 1] His statement: 'Before the war lays down its burdens' is an adaptation from His statement, the Exalted: 'Then either a favor after or ransom until the war lays down its burdens' meaning its instruments and heavy loads without which war cannot be carried out, such as weapons and horses, and it is an indication of the end of war and cessation from it. (4)
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary on the ruling of ransoming captives (fida') in jihad, refining earlier commentaries. The author clarifies the Hanafi position on when and how ransom is permissible. The key distinction is timing: before the war ends, ransom with money is allowed, but with Muslim captives it is not. After the war ends, ransom with money is prohibited by consensus of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), and ransom with a Muslim captive is prohibited according to Abu Hanifa but permitted by the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The text then presents multiple narrations and opinions. Al-Karkhi restricts Abu Yusuf's permission to before division of booty, while Muhammad allows it absolutely. Al-Zayla'i and al-Kamal ibn al-Humam consider the permissibility of ransom with Muslim captives as the preferred view, supported by a hadith in Sahih Muslim. The final relied-upon position (mufta bihi) from Radd al-Muhtar is that prohibition is only for ransom with money when there is no need; but ransom with money in case of need, or with Muslim captives, is permissible. The verse from Surah Muhammad (47:4) is cited, showing that the option of ransom is conditioned by 'until the war lays down its burdens,' implying that after the war the option ends. The Hanafi school restricts the application of this verse accordingly.

Key Terms
فداء (fida'): Ransom paid for the release of a captive, which may be money or a Muslim captive exchanged.
أسير (aseer): A captive taken in jihad, either Muslim or non-Muslim.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): The abode of war, i.e., non-Muslim territory where jihad is conducted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is the ruling on ransoming a captive with money after the war ends?
A) Absolutely prohibited
B) Permissible, but only before division of booty
C) Prohibited unless there is a need (hajah)
D) Permissible unconditionally

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits ransoming captives with money after war ends, but permits it when need arises, and permits exchanging Muslim captives according to the preferred view.

Prohibited Actions in Dar al-Harb: Returning Captives, Maiming Animals, and Dividing Booty
Commentary on three prohibitions from Al-Hidayah with ta'lil and a madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited actions in dar al-harb, explain the Hanafi rationale for each prohibition, and identify the differing views on dividing booty.

Core Idea
Maiming animals, returning captives, and dividing booty in enemy territory are prohibited to avoid strengthening the enemy and causing unnecessary harm.

This passage from Al-Hidayah, expanded by 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, presents three key prohibitions in dar al-harb. Understanding these rulings reveals the ethical and strategic principles underlying Hanafi jihad law. The commentary provides both the rulings and their underlying reasons (ta'lil), as well as noting internal and external differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Actions
List the three actions that the text declares prohibited: (1) returning captives to their homes, (2) maiming animals that are difficult to transport, and (3) dividing booty before returning to dar al-Islam.
These are all mentioned in the matn as part of the negation: 'it is not permissible'.
2
Locate the Ruling and its Proof
For each action, note the ruling (prohibited) and the evidence or rationale given. The text provides ta'lil (causation) rather than explicit scriptural proof. For returning captives: because it strengthens the enemy. For maiming: because it is mutilation (muthla) and torture without necessity. For dividing booty: because the booty is not yet secure and proper distribution requires the imam's agency.
The text does not cite a Quranic verse or hadith directly but refers to the general prohibition of muthla and the principle of avoiding strengthening the enemy.
3
Understand the Ta'lil for Maiming vs. Slaughter and Burning
The text distinguishes between maiming (which is forbidden) and slaughter followed by burning (permitted). The rationale: maiming is mutilation and causes unnecessary suffering, while slaughter is a permissible method of killing and burning prevents the enemy from benefiting from the carcass. Burning without prior slaughter is also prohibited because it involves torture.
This shows Hanafi attention to both the method and the outcome.
4
Analyze the Dispute on Dividing Booty
The main Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, and one narration from Abu Yusuf) prohibits division in dar al-harb. Muhammad allows it, and Abu Yusuf has two narrations. Outside the school, al-Shafi'i allows it absolutely. The madhhab dispute map in the toolbox provides the details. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf): if the imam divides in dar al-harb, the division is invalid according to the relied-upon view.
The text highlights that the prohibition is based on blocking potential mischief and ensuring booty is distributed under proper authority.
5
Apply the Ruling to a Hypothetical Scenario
Consider an imam who conquers a fort in dar al-harb and captures livestock. He faces difficulty transporting them. According to the Hanafi ruling, he should slaughter and burn the animals, not maim them. He should also not distribute the booty among the soldiers until they return to dar al-Islam.
This step solidifies the practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجهاد / باب المغنم وقسمته
وردهم إلى دارهم، وعَقْرُ دابة يشق نقلها وذُبِحَتْ وحُرقَتْ ، وقُسْمَةً مغنم ويجوز عند محمد الله ، وعن أبي يوسف الله روايتان ، وعند الشَّافِعِي) يجوز مطلقاً
[١]قوله : يجوز مطلقاً ؛ سواء كان بالمال أو بالنفس، وسواء كان قبل الفراغ من الحرب أو بعده.
[٢) قوله : وردّهم إلى دارهم ؛ معطوف على منهم»، كما أن قوله : «وعقر»، وقوله : «وقسمته» معطوف عليه، وكلّها داخلةٌ تحت النفي، يعني لا يجوز أن يردّ الأسارى إلى دارهم ؛ لأن فيه تقوية لأهل الكفر.
[٣] قوله : وعقر دابة...الخ ؛ العَقرُ - بالفتح - يقال : عقر الناقة بالسيف ضربَ قوائمها، وقطعها، يعني إذا أراد الإمام العود بعسكره من دار الحرب إلى داره ومعه دواب ومواشي يشق عليه نقلها لا يجوز له أن يعقرها ويتركها هناك، فإنّ في العقر تعذيب الحيوان من غير ضرورة، وهو أيضاً مثلة، وقد نهى عنها.
بل يذبحها ويحرقها بالنار لتقطع منفعة الكفّار بهما ، وصار كتخريب البنيان بخلاف التحريق قبل الذبح ، فإنّه منهي عنه ، وتحرق الأسلحة أيضاً، وما لا يحترق منها يدفن في موضع لا يطلع عليه الكفّار، كذا في «الهداية»(۳).
[٤]قوله : وقسمة مغنم.... الخ ؛ توضيح المقام على ما في «الهداية»(4) وحواشيها : إنه لا يجوز للإمام أن يقسّم غنيمته في دار الحرب حتى يخرجها إلى دار الإسلام، وقال الشافعي : لا بأس به.
The Book of Jihad / Chapter on Booty and Its Division. 'And returning them to their homes, and maiming an animal whose transport is difficult until it is slaughtered and burned, and dividing booty.' And it is permissible according to Muhammad, and from Abu Yusuf there are two narrations, and according to al-Shafi'i it is permissible absolutely. [1] His statement: 'It is permissible absolutely' — whether with money or with a person, and whether before cessation of war or after. [2] His statement: 'And returning them to their homes' is a conjunction to 'from them', just as his statement 'and maiming' and his statement 'and its division' are conjoined to it, and all fall under negation, meaning it is not permissible to return the captives to their homes because that strengthens the people of disbelief. [3] His statement: 'And maiming an animal...' — al-'aqr (with fatha) is said: he maimed the she-camel with a sword, striking and cutting its legs. It means if the imam wishes to return with his army from dar al-harb to his home and he has animals and livestock whose transport is difficult, it is not permissible for him to maim and leave them there, because in maiming there is torture of the animal without necessity, and it is also mutilation (muthla), which has been prohibited. Rather, he should slaughter them and burn them with fire to cut off the benefit of the disbelievers from them, and it becomes like demolishing buildings, unlike burning before slaughter, for that is prohibited. Weapons are also burned, and what does not burn from them is buried in a place where the disbelievers will not find it. Thus in al-Hidayah (3). [4] His statement: 'And dividing booty...' — clarification of the matter based on al-Hidayah (4) and its glosses: it is not permissible for the imam to divide his booty in dar al-harb until he brings it out to dar al-Islam. Al-Shafi'i said: There is no harm in it.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn from al-Hidayah concerning three prohibited actions in dar al-harb. First, returning captives to their homes (dar al-harb) is prohibited because it strengthens the enemy. Second, maiming (al-'aqr) an animal that is difficult to transport is prohibited because it constitutes torture of animals without necessity and is a form of mutilation (muthla), which the Prophet (PBUH) forbade. Instead, the imam should slaughter the animal and then burn it (or burn weapons and bury non-combustibles) to prevent the enemy from benefiting. Note that burning before slaughter is separately prohibited. Third, dividing booty (ghanima) in dar al-harb is not permissible until it is brought to dar al-Islam. This is the Hanafi position, though Muhammad allows it, and from Abu Yusuf there are two narrations (permission and prohibition). Imam al-Shafi'i allows it absolutely. The underlying reasons (ta'lil) are: for returning captives, it strengthens the enemy; for maiming, it is unnecessary cruelty; for dividing booty, it ensures proper distribution under the imam's authority and prevents discord.

Key Terms
عقر ('aqr): The act of cutting an animal's legs with a sword, i.e., maiming it.
مثلة (muthla): Mutilation of a dead body or living being, forbidden in Islamic law.
غنيمة (ghanima): Booty taken from the enemy in war, subject to division rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is returning captives to their homes in dar al-harb prohibited?
A) Because it is a form of mutilation
B) Because it strengthens the enemy
C) Because it delays the division of booty
D) Because it is not necessary

Key Takeaway
In dar al-harb, the Hanafi school prohibits returning captives (strengthens the enemy), maiming animals (mutilation), and dividing booty (until safe return), with slaughter and burning permitted for animals.

Division of Spoils in Dar al-Harb: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute on whether spoils must be transferred to Dar al-Islam before division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on dividing spoils in Dar al-Harb, identify the conditions for validity, and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Ownership of spoils requires transfer to Dar al-Islam, but division may be valid under ijtihad or need.

The Prophet ﷺ divided spoils both after returning to Medina and in conquered lands. The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ on whether division in enemy territory is valid. This lesson unpacks the proofs, the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and the conditions that make division valid.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the default ruling from the passage: division in Dar al-Harb is not preferred but permissible under certain conditions. Note the ikhtilaf among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
Muhammad considers it makruh tanzihi; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider it not permissible.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i school holds that ownership is established by mere domination (istila) in enemy territory, so division is valid without transfer.
Their analogy: hunting and gathering firewood.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i argues that istila over permissible, unprotected wealth transfers ownership immediately, regardless of location.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that domination requires both a preserving hand and a transferring hand. In enemy territory, the transferring hand is absent due to enemy ability to reclaim.
They cite the Prophet's practice: division after securing the land.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If division is validated in Dar al-Harb, all consequences (halal intercourse, sale, manumission, inheritance) apply. Otherwise, they are suspended until ihraz.
This has practical implications for soldiers and their families.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عندنا ، أن ملك الغانمين لا يثبتُ قبل الإحراز بدار الإسلام. ومنشأ الخلاف هوا وعنده يثبت له أن سبب الملك الاستيلاء الوارد على مال مباح غير معصوم، كما في ملك الصيد والاحتطاب ، وقد تحقق الاستيلاء بثبوت يد أهل الإسلام، فيثبت الملك من دون نقل إلى بلد الإسلام، فيجوز للإمام أن يقسم بين الغانمين هناك.
ولنا : إنّ الاستيلاء عبارة عن إثباتِ اليد الحافظة والناقلة، والثاني مفقود ما دام الإمام في دارهم ؛ لقدرتهم على استخلاص أموالهم من أهل الإسلام، فإن الدار دارهم، بخلاف ما إذا فتحت البلدة عنوة.
وقال أبو يوسف له في كتاب «الخراج»: «إذا غنم المسلمون غنيمة من أهل الشرك فأحب إلي أن لا يقسم حتى يخرج من دار الحرب إلى دار الإسلام، وإن قسمت في دار الحرب جاز، والقسمة خارج دار الحرب أفضل، فإنّها ليست بمحرزة ما دامت في دار الحرب. وقد قسم رسول الله ﷺ غنائم بدر بعد منصرفه إلى المدينة، وضرب لعثمان بن عفان رضي الله عنه فيها بسهم وكان خلفه على رقية بنت رسول الله ﷺ وهي زوجته، وكانت مريضة، وضرب لطلحة بن عبيد الله رضي الله عنه فيها بسهم، ولم يكن حضر الواقعة، وكان بالشام.
وجرى (1) وكان رسول الله ﷺ قسم غنائم خيبر بخيبر، لكنه لما ظهر عليها وأجلى عنها أهلها صارت مثل دار الإسلام، وقسّم غنائم بني المصطلق في بلادهم؛ لأنه كان افتتحها، حكمه عليها، فكان القسم فيها بمنزلة القسم في المدينة». انتهى وهذا صريح في أن القسمة في دار الحرب خلافُ الأفضل، ولو فعل جاز. وفي «الهداية»: «قيل : موضعُ الخلافِ - أي بيننا وبين الشافعي – ترتب الأحكام على القسمة، إذا قَسَّمَ الإمامُ لا عن اجتهاد ؛ لأنّ حكم الملك لا يثبت بدونه ، وقيل : الكراهة ، وهي كراهة تنزيهية عند محمد رحمه الله ، فإنّه قال على قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف لا تجوز القسمة في دار الحرب ، وعند محمد رحمه الله الأفضل أن يُقسم في دارِ الإسلام.
ووجه الكراهة : إن دليل البطلان راجع إلى أنه تقاعد عن الجواز، فلا يتقاعد عن إيراثِ الكراهة». انتهى وذكر في «المحيط» و«الفتح» (3) وغيرهما : إنّ القسمة تجوز في دار الحرب اتفاقاً إذا قسم الإمام عن اجتهاد أو لحاجة الغزاة أو ما إذا طلبوا منه القسمة وخشي الفتنة فتصح القسمة وتثبتُ الأحكام المرتبة على القسمة من حلّ الوطء والبيع والعتق والإرث ، بخلاف ما قبل القسمة بدون اجتهاد أو احتياج، ولو بعد الإحراز بدارنا. (1) قوله : إلا إيداعاً؛ قال في «مختصر القُدُوري»: إن لم تكن للإمام حمولة يحتمل عليها الغنائم قسمها بين الغانمين قسمة إيداع ليحملوها إلى دار الإسلام، ثم يرتجعها منهم فيقسمها. انتهى. قال في «الهداية»: «هكذا ذكر في «المختصر » ولم يشترط رضاهم، وهو رواية «السير الكبير»، والجملة في هذا : إنّ الإمام إذا وجد في المغنم حمولة يحمل الغنائم عليها ؛ لأنّ الحمولة والمحمولة مالهم ، وكذا إذا كان في بيت المال فضل حمولة ؛ لأنه مال المسلمين. ولو كان للغانمين أو لبعضهم لا يجبرهم في رواية السير الصغير» ؛ لأنه ابتداءً إجارة، وصار كما إذا نفقت دابة في مفازة، ومع رفيقه فضل حمولة، ويجبرهم في رواية «السير الكبير ؛ لأنه دفع الضرر العام بتحميل ضرر خاص [2] قوله : وردء؛ - بكسر الراء المهملة وسكون الدال المهملة، ثمّ همزة - هو العون ؛ أي المعين، - وبفتح الراء - مصدر يقال : ردأه ردء : أعانه.
(1) وصورتها أن لا يكون لإمام من بيت المال ما يحمل عليه الغنيمة، فيقسمها بين الغانمين ليحملوها إلى دار الإسلام ، ثم يرتجعها. ينظر : فتح باب العناية»(3 : 277).
(2) من «الهداية (5 : 480-481).
(3) «فتح القدير» (5 : 481).
(4) انتهى من «الهداية»(5 : 483-484).
According to us (Hanafis): The ownership of the spoils is not established before transfer (ihraz) to Dar al-Islam. The origin of the dispute is that according to him (Shafi'i) ownership is established because the cause of ownership is domination (istila) over permissible, unprotected wealth, as in ownership of hunting and gathering wood. Domination is realized by the establishment of the hand of the Muslims, so ownership is established without transfer to the land of Islam, so it is permissible for the Imam to divide among the spoils-takers there. Our proof: Domination is an expression of establishing both the preserving hand and the transferring hand, and the second is lacking as long as the Imam is in their land, due to their ability to reclaim their wealth from the Muslims, for the land is their land, unlike when the town is conquered by force. Abu Yusuf said in Kitab al-Kharaj: 'When Muslims take spoils from polytheists, I prefer that they not divide until they leave Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam. But if they divide in Dar al-Harb, it is permissible, and division outside Dar al-Harb is better, for it is not secured (muhraz) as long as it is in Dar al-Harb. The Messenger of Allah ﷺ divided the spoils of Badr after his return to Medina, and gave a share to Uthman ibn Affan (may Allah be pleased with him) although he was left behind with Ruqayyah bint the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, who was his wife and was sick, and gave a share to Talhah ibn Ubaydullah (may Allah be pleased with him) although he was not present at the battle, being in Syria. And (the narration continues): The Messenger of Allah ﷺ divided the spoils of Khaybar at Khaybar, but when he conquered it and expelled its inhabitants, it became like Dar al-Islam. And he divided the spoils of Banu al-Mustaliq in their land because he had conquered it, having authority over it, so division there was like division in Medina.' End quote. This is explicit that division in Dar al-Harb is contrary to the better, but if done, it is permissible. In al-Hidayah: 'It is said: The point of dispute – between us and al-Shafi'i – is the attachment of rulings to the division, if the Imam divides without ijtihad, because the ruling of ownership is not established without it. And it is said: it is dislike (karaha), and it is a tanzihi dislike according to Muhammad, for he said: According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, division in Dar al-Harb is not permissible, and according to Muhammad, it is better to divide in Dar al-Islam. The basis of the dislike: The evidence of nullity is that it falls short of permissibility, so it does not fall short of causing dislike.' End quote. In al-Muhit and Fath al-Qadir and others it is mentioned: Division is permissible in Dar al-Harb by agreement if the Imam divides based on ijtihad, or for the need of the ghuzat, or if they request division and he fears fitna, so the division is valid and the rulings attached to division from permissibility of intercourse, sale, manumission, and inheritance are established, unlike division without ijtihad or need, even after transfer to our Dar. [1] His saying: 'except as a deposit'; said in Mukhtasar al-Quduri: 'If the Imam does not have beasts to carry the spoils, he divides them among the ghuzat as a deposit division so that they carry them to Dar al-Islam, then he retrieves them from them and divides them.' End quote. Al-Hidayah said: 'Thus it is mentioned in al-Mukhtasar, and he did not condition their consent, and it is a narration of al-Siyar al-Kabir. The summary: If the Imam finds in the spoils beasts to carry the spoils upon them, because the beasts and the carried goods are their property, and likewise if there is surplus of beasts in the treasury, because it is the property of Muslims. If the beasts belong to the ghuzat or some of them, he does not compel them in the narration of al-Siyar al-Saghir, because it is an initial hiring, and it becomes like when a beast dies in a desert and his companion has surplus of beasts; but he compels them in the narration of al-Siyar al-Kabir, because it is repelling general harm by imposing a specific harm.' [2] His saying: 'wa rad'; with kasr of the ra, sukun of the da, then hamza; it means 'aid', i.e., the helper. With fatha of the ra, it is a masdar: 'rada'ahu rad'an: he aided him.' (1) Its description: that the Imam does not have from the treasury what to carry the spoils upon, so he divides it among the ghuzat to carry it to Dar al-Islam, then retrieves it. Reference: Fath Bab al-Inayah (3:277). (2) From al-Hidayah (5:480-481). (3) Fath al-Qadir (5:481). (4) End quote from al-Hidayah (5:483-484).
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the validity of dividing spoils (ghanimah) in Dar al-Harb before transferring them to Dar al-Islam. The Hanafi position, presented first, is that ownership of spoils is not established until they are brought to Dar al-Islam (ihraz). The Shafi'i view, stated briefly, is that ownership is established by mere domination (istila) in Dar al-Harb, analogous to hunting or gathering firewood, thus making division permissible immediately. The Hanafis respond that domination requires both a preserving hand (yad hafiza) and a transferring hand (yad naqila), and the latter is lacking in enemy territory because the enemy can reclaim the spoils. This is unlike conquest (anwatan), where full control is established. The passage then cites Abu Yusuf's opinion from Kitab al-Kharaj: he prefers delaying division until return to Dar al-Islam, but if done in Dar al-Harb it is permissible. He supports this by noting that the Prophet ﷺ divided the spoils of Badr after returning to Medina, and at Khaybar after securing the land. These examples show that division in enemy territory is contrary to the better (khilaf al-afdal) but valid. The text then quotes al-Hidayah, which clarifies that the point of dispute is not the permissibility itself but whether legal consequences (like permissibility of intercourse, sale, etc.) attach to a division made without ijtihad. According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, division in Dar al-Harb is makruh tanzihi (mildly disliked), while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it is not permissible (la tujiz). The later sources (al-Muhit, Fath al-Qadir) reconcile this by stating that division is agreed to be valid if the Imam acts with ijtihad, for necessity, or at the request of the soldiers to avoid fitna. In such cases, the division is valid and all subsequent rulings apply. The passage also discusses the exceptional 'deposit division' when transport is unavailable, and defines the term 'rad' (support) in the marginal note.

Key Terms
إحراز (ihraz): Taking possession of spoils by bringing them to Dar al-Islam, ensuring security from enemy recovery.
قسمة (qisma): Division of spoils among those entitled (ghuzat), can be either deposit division (qismat al-ida') or final division (qismat al-tamlik).
ردء (rad'): Support, aid; in the context, it refers to additional soldiers or assistance sent to reinforce the army.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on dividing spoils in Dar al-Harb when the Imam has not made ijtihad and there is no need?
A) Absolutely forbidden (haram)
B) Permissible (mubah)
C) Disliked (makruh tanzihi)
D) Invalid (batil)

Key Takeaway
Division of spoils in Dar al-Harb is valid in the Hanafi school if the Imam acts with ijtihad or for need; otherwise it is disliked but not invalid.
