Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
6 min
Division of Spoils in Dar al-Harb: From Karaha to Conditional Permissibility
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing ghanimah in Dar al-Harb with conditional permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions under which division of ghanimah in Dar al-Harb is valid according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, and explain why the default ruling is makruh.

Core Idea
Division of spoils in Dar al-Harb is makruh but becomes valid with ijtihad, need, or fear of fitna.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the permissibility of dividing spoils while still in enemy territory. Their disagreement is resolved by later authorities who agree that division is valid under specific conditions. Understanding this ruling requires tracing the reasoning from the default karaha to the conditional permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the basic dispute
The act is dividing ghanimah (spoils) in Dar al-Harb (enemy territory). Abu Yusuf holds it is not permissible at all; Imam Muhammad says it is better to delay until Dar al-Islam. Both consider the default ruling to be disliked (makruh).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between the two main disciples of Abu Hanifa.
2
Understand the default ruling (karaha) and its proof
The default is makruh because the evidence of invalidity (bultan) prevents the act from being permissible, but it does not prevent causing dislike. This talil (legal reasoning) explains why the act is disliked even if it might be invalid in some cases.
The text says: 'دليل البطلان راجع إلى أنه تقاعد عن الجواز، فلا يتقاعد عن إيراث الكراهة'.
3
Recognize the conditions that override the default
According to al-Muhit, al-Fath, and others, division becomes valid by agreement (ittifaq) when: (1) the Imam divides based on ijtihad, (2) the ghazis have a need, or (3) they request division and the Imam fears fitna (discord).
These three conditions are alternative; any one suffices for validity.
4
Determine the legal consequences of a valid division
When division is valid, all rulings of ownership are established: the spoils become permissible for intercourse (for female captives), sale, emancipation, and inheritance among the recipients.
These consequences only apply after a valid division; before division, the spoils remain collectively owned and such actions are not allowed.
5
Apply the ruling: distinguish between valid and invalid scenarios
If the division occurs without one of the three conditions, it is invalid—even if the spoils have already been transported to Dar al-Islam. The default makruh applies only when the act is performed without conditions, but the act itself is invalid.
The passage explicitly states: 'بخلاف ما قبل القسمة بدون اجتهاد أو احتياج، ولو بعد الإحراز بدارنا'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يوسف لا تجوز القسمة في دار الحرب، وعند محمد الأفضل أن يُقسم في دار الإسلام. ووجه الكراهة: إن دليل البطلان راجع إلى أنه تقاعد عن الجواز، فلا يتقاعد عن إيراث الكراهة. انتهى. وذكر في «المحيط» و«الفتح» وغيرهما: إن القسمة تجوز في دار الحرب اتفاقاً إذا قسم الإمام عن اجتهاد أو لحاجة الغزاة أو ما إذا طلبوا منه القسمة وخشي الفتنة فتصح القسمة وتثبت الأحكام المرتبة على القسمة من حل الوطء والبيع والعتق والإرث، بخلاف ما قبل القسمة بدون اجتهاد أو احتياج، ولو بعد الإحراز بدارنا.
Abu Yusuf: division is not permissible in Dar al-Harb. Muhammad: it is better to divide in Dar al-Islam. The reason for dislike: the proof of invalidity returns to its prevention of permissibility, so it does not prevent causing dislike. End. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit and al-Fath and others: division is permissible in Dar al-Harb by agreement if the Imam divides based on ijtihad or due to the need of the ghazis, or if they request division from him and he fears discord. Then the division is valid and the rulings connected to division from permissibility of intercourse, sale, emancipation, and inheritance are established. Unlike before division without ijtihad or need, even after transport to our land.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on dividing spoils (ghanimah) while still in enemy territory (Dar al-Harb). It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that division is not permissible at all in Dar al-Harb, while Imam Muhammad deems it better to delay division until reaching Dar al-Islam. The text then explains the basis for the dislike (karaha): the legal cause indicating invalidity (bultan) prevents the act from being fully permissible, but does not prevent it from being disliked. However, a consensus (ittifaq) from later authorities (al-Muhit, al-Fath) allows division in Dar al-Harb under specific conditions: the Imam must act on his own ijtihad, or there must be a need for the ghazis, or they must request division and the Imam fears discord. In such cases, division is valid and all consequences like lawful sexual relations, sale, emancipation, and inheritance take effect. Without these conditions, division is invalid even if the spoils have been transported to Dar al-Islam.

Key Terms
الغنيمة (al-ghanimah): Spoils taken from the enemy by force during war.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim control where Islamic law does not prevail.
الكراهة (al-karahah): Legal dislike; here it implies makruh tahrimi (close to forbidden) in the default case.
دليل البطلان (dalil al-bultan): Evidence indicating invalidity of the act; here it refers to the legal reasoning that prevents permissibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, when is division of spoils in Dar al-Harb valid?
A) Only when the Imam acts on ijtihad
B) When the Imam acts on ijtihad, or the ghazis need it, or they request and he fears fitna
C) It is never valid in Dar al-Harb
D) Only if the spoils have been moved to Dar al-Islam

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits division of spoils in Dar al-Harb under ijtihad, need, or request and fear of fitna, overriding the default karaha.
